   E.   Prevent any person from using any part or any of its facilities or
interfere with such use in compliance with this Chapter and the rules and
regulations applicable to such use.
   F.   Violate any rules and regulations for the use of a park or any of its
facilities, approved by the Council of the City or its duly authorized
representative.
   G.   Solicit or accost other persons for the purpose of begging or
soliciting alms.
   H.   Operate or aid in the operation of private radios, stereophonic or
sound-amplification devices at a level creating a nuisance to the general
public. (1993 Code)
5-3-5: MERCHANDISING, ADVERTISING AND SIGNS:
No person in any park shall:
   A.   Vending and Peddling: Expose or offer for sale any article or thing,
nor shall he station or place any stand, cart or vehicle for the
transportation, sale or display of any such article or thing. Exception is
hereby made as to any regularly licensed concessionaire acting by and under the
authority and regulation of the City Council or any authorized representative.
   B.   Advertising: Distribute, leave or throw any advertising material, such
as dodgers, handbills, circulars or like matter or give away or otherwise
distribute for advertising purposes any goods or wares.
   C.   Signs: Paste, glue, tack or otherwise post any signs, plaques,
advertisements or inscriptions whatever, except plaques, tablets or signs of a
size, design and location approved by the City Council or duly authorized
representative, recognizing or acknowledging donations or contributions to any
City park or public facilities therein. (1993 Code)
5-3-6: PARK OPERATING POLICY; HOURS:
Except for unusual and unforeseen emergencies, parks shall be open to the
public every day of the year from six o'clock (6:00) A.M. to twelve o'clock
(12:00) midnight. Thereafter, visitors and vehicles shall be excluded during
the hours of closure except for transit through a park. (1993 Code)
5-3-7: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Enforcement Officials: Officials, police officers or duly authorized
representatives of the City Council shall enforce the provisions of this
Chapter.
   B.   Ejectment: A police officer or a duly authorized representative of the
City Council shall have the authority to eject from the park any person acting
in violation of this Chapter.
   C.   Seizure of Property: A police officer shall have the authority to seize
and confiscate any property, thing or device in the park used in violation of
this Chapter. (1993 Code)
5-3-8: PENALTIES:
Any person found to be violating any provision of this Chapter shall be guilty
of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to penalties
provided in Section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1993 Code)
CHAPTER 4
TREES AND SHRUBS
SECTION:
5-4-1: Title
5-4-2: Purpose
5-4-3: Definitions
5-4-4: Establishment Of Plummer Tree Committee
5-4-5: Authority And Control Over Trees
5-4-6: Removal Of Public Trees And Shrubs
5-4-7: Planting Of Public Trees And Shrubs
5-4-8: Permit Required
5-4-9: Appeal Procedures
5-4-10: Damaging, Destroying Or Topping Of Public Trees Or Shrubs
5-4-11: Care Of Trees Within City
5-4-12: Public Nuisances
5-4-13: Penalty
5-4-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be titled as the PLUMMER TREE ORDINANCE.
(Ord. 358, 1-8-2004)
5-4-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to protect trees and shrubs planted and growing
within the public rights of way, city parks, and within or on all other
property owned or otherwise under the control of the city; to establish and
maintain species variety and age diversity of trees on public lands in the
city; to maintain city trees in a healthy and nonhazardous condition through
standard arboricultural practices. (Ord. 358, 1-8-2004)
5-4-3: DEFINITIONS:
COMMUNITY FOREST: Trees and shrubs on public and private property within the
community.
DAMAGES: Injury or harm that impairs the health, vigor, value, or usefulness of
a tree, as determined by the Plummer tree committee.
OWNER: The person (the legal owner, tenant, occupant or lessee) who exercises
care, custody or control of private real property that abuts a right of way
upon which a public tree or shrub is located.
PARK TREE: Any tree within the boundaries of a designated city park.
PARKWAY: That portion of a street between a roadway and sidewalk.
PERSON: Any individual, firm, copartnership, association, corporation, or group
acting as a unit.
PUBLIC PROPERTY: Property owned by the city of Plummer either in fee simple
absolute, or implied, or expressly dedicated to the public for present or
future use for purposes of vehicular or pedestrian traffic, or for public
easements.
PUBLIC TREE OR SHRUB: Any tree or shrub that is situated in such a manner that
fifty one percent (51%) or more of the tree trunk or shrub base at ground level
is on public property or public right of way.
ROADWAY: The portion of a street improved, designed or ordinarily used by the
public for vehicular travel.
SHRUB: A multiple stemmed, woody plant whose height at maturity is between two
feet (2') and fifteen feet (15').
SIDEWALK: That portion of a street improved, designed or ordinarily used by the
public for pedestrian travel.
STREET: The entire width between the boundary lines of a public right of way
dedicated or deeded to the city for use of the public for purposes of vehicular
travel, whether or not maintained by the city and whether or not open for
vehicular traffic.
STREET TREE: Any tree, shrub or other woody vegetation on lands within any city
right of way.
TOPPING: The severe cutting back of limbs within a tree crown to such a degree
that only stubs remain or the removal of the top part (trunk and limbs) of a
coniferous tree, thereby removing a significant portion of the normal crown.
TREE: A woody perennial plant with one main stem or trunk. (Ord. 358, 1-8-2004)
5-4-4: ESTABLISHMENT OF PLUMMER TREE COMMITTEE:
   A.   Plummer Tree Committee: There is hereby created a Plummer tree
committee. The Plummer tree committee shall consist of a minimum of five (5)
volunteer members who are residents of this community, including a chairperson.
City council members and city employees may be appointed as committee members.
Members of the committee shall be appointed by the mayor with the approval of
the city council to serve three (3) year appointments, without compensation,
with staggered terms to provide continuity and transition within the committee.
A city council member shall be appointed to serve as council liaison.
   B.   Duties And Responsibilities Of Committee Members: It shall be the
responsibility of the Plummer tree committee to:
      1.   Study, investigate, develop and update a written plan for the
selection, care, preservation, pruning, planting, replanting, removal or
disposition of trees and shrubs in the public streets and all other public
property or rights of way. Such plan will be presented to the city council and
upon their acceptance and approval, shall constitute the official comprehensive
city tree plan for the city of Plummer.
      2.   Distribute guidelines for the pruning of trees located on all city
properties and within city rights of way.
      3.   Distribute a tree list consisting of acceptable varieties of trees,
acceptable size of trees, proper planting and spacing instructions for trees
located within the rights of way.
      4.   Assist the city in providing information to the public through
published materials, workshops, on site consultations, and other educational
opportunities.
      5.   Identify landscaping projects that improve the community forest.
      6.   Assist the city in planning and implementing Arbor Day celebrations
and activities.
      7.   Review tree permit applications for planting and removal of public
trees.
      8.   Approve or deny tree permit applications for planting and removal of
public trees by issuance of a written permit or denial in writing.
      9.   Oversee planting, pruning, spraying, preserving and removal of trees
on all public properties and rights of way.
      10.   Review the city tree program budget and make recommendations to the
city council.
      11.   Encourage and solicit donations and other funding for the city tree
program.
      12.   Conduct regular monthly meetings, or as needed, to review permit
applications, plan city tree activities, and otherwise implement the provisions
of this chapter.
   C.   Duties And Responsibilities Of Committee Chairperson: It shall be the
responsibility of the Plummer tree committee chairperson to:
      1.   Preside over Plummer tree committee meetings and report activities
to the council liaison.
      2.   Organize materials for public education and distribution.
      3.   Accept applications for tree permits for review by the committee.
      4.   Keep an accurate record of permit applications and the disposition
of each. (Ord. 358, 1-8-2004)
5-4-5: AUTHORITY AND CONTROL OVER TREES:
The mayor and city council have complete authority and control over all trees
on or within the city properties. The city, with advice from the Plummer tree
committee may remove or cause the removal of public or private trees or
branches which create a hazard to public health and safety or public trees
which should be removed to implement community forestry objectives. (Ord. 358,
1-8-2004)
5-4-6: REMOVAL OF PUBLIC TREES AND SHRUBS:
It is the policy of the city of Plummer that public trees and shrubs shall not
be removed without a written permit from the Plummer tree committee. Permits
will be granted pursuant to the criteria specified below:
   A.   The tree or shrub is sufficiently diseased or is an alternate host of a
significant disease.
   B.   The tree or shrub is harboring injurious insects or pathogens and may
cause significant potential danger to the community forest.
   C.   The tree or shrub is dead or near dead and/or constitutes a public
safety hazard.
   D.   The tree interferes with overhead utility lines and creates a public
safety hazard.
   E.   The tree or shrub causes sight obstruction that cannot be resolved in a
more moderate manner.
   F.   The replacement plan for removed trees and shrubs.
   G.   Any other criteria deemed appropriate by the Plummer tree committee.
(Ord. 358, 1-8-2004)
5-4-7: PLANTING OF PUBLIC TREES AND SHRUBS:
It is the policy of the city of Plummer that public trees and shrubs shall not
be planted without a written permit from the Plummer tree committee. Permits
will be granted pursuant to the criteria specified below:
   A.   The location of the proposed planting in relation to existing or future
utility lines.
   B.   The species of the proposed planting, its expected height, and its root
system in relation to existing or future utility lines.
   C.   The location and species in relation to the line of sight for traffic.
   D.   Any other criteria deemed appropriate by the Plummer tree committee.
(Ord. 358, 1-8-2004)
5-4-8: PERMIT REQUIRED:
   A.   It is unlawful for any person to plant or remove any trees or shrubs on
or within the public properties without first procuring a permit from the tree
committee. In situations where imminent public danger would result from the
delay entailed in obtaining a permit or where such delay would place life, limb
or property in jeopardy, the city may waive the permit requirement.
   B.   Any person desiring a permit to plant or remove a tree or shrub on or
within the city properties shall file with the city clerk or tree committee
chairperson an application to do so.
   C.   Permits shall be provided at no cost.
   D.   Applications to plant a tree or shrub must identify the proposed tree
or shrub. Selection and location of required replacement trees and shrubs shall
be subject to the approval of the Plummer tree committee.
   E.   Upon the filing of such application, the tree committee shall
investigate the proposed work and, if in their judgment it is desirable and
should be done, shall issue a written permit. Denial of a permit shall be
issued in writing.
   F.   In addition to a permit, a temporary street closure approval from the
city is required whenever such tree work will impair the free and full use of
any sidewalk, street or alley as determined by the city public works foreman.
   G.   If a permit for removal is justified, the tree committee shall issue a
removal permit. Work may be supervised and inspected by the committee
chairperson or his or her agent. All costs of the removal shall be at the
expense of the applicant. Whenever a public tree or shrub is removed, as a
condition of issuance of a permit for removal, the applicant shall replace the
tree or shrub removed, unless such requirement is waived by the Plummer tree
committee for good cause showing. Selection and location of required
replacement trees and shrubs shall be subject to the approval of the Plummer
tree committee. (Ord. 358, 1-8-2004)
5-4-9: APPEAL PROCEDURES:
   A.   Any applicant may appeal the decision of the Plummer tree committee in
the denial of a permit under this chapter to the Plummer city council. A
request for an appeal hearing shall be in writing and submitted to the city
clerk. An appeal of a decision of the Plummer tree committee must be filed
within fourteen (14) days from the date of the adverse decision. The hearing
before the council shall take place within thirty (30) days from the filing of
the appeal.
   B.   When the hearing is conducted the applicant may be in attendance and/or
he or she may be represented. The hearing will be informal. The hearing will be
open to the public. The evidence presented by either party may consist of
relevant physical evidence and testimony, but the rules of evidence shall not
apply. Upon completion of the hearing, the council shall take under advisement
all evidence presented and shall notify the applicant in writing within
fourteen (14) days from the hearing of its findings and ruling, which shall
affirm, overturn or modify the action of the tree committee. (Ord. 358, 1-8-
2004)
5-4-10: DAMAGING, DESTROYING OR TOPPING OF PUBLIC TREES OR SHRUBS:
It is unlawful for any person to:
   A.   Damage, mutilate or destroy any public tree or shrub of the city.
   B.   Store or place, or cause to be stored or placed: oil, gasoline,
chemicals and other materials that are harmful to trees and shrubs, around or
near public trees and shrubs.
   C.   Spill or dump substances, whether liquid or solid, which are toxic to
trees and shrubs, on the soil between the base of the public tree and the
extent of its root system.
   D.   Attach a potentially harmful device or structure (i.e., tree houses,
signs, etc.) to or on public trees unless otherwise authorized by the city.
   E.   Make excavations in the soil near roots of public trees or shrubs
unless appropriate measures are taken to prevent exposed soil from drying out.
   F.   Damage roots of a public tree or shrub by compacting or filling on or
around the base of the tree.
   G.   Damage a public tree or shrub by the practice of "topping", except
under special circumstances. Trees severely damaged by storms or other causes,
or certain trees under utility wires or other obstructions where other pruning
practices are impractical may be exempted from this section at the
determination of the Plummer tree committee, based upon good cause therefor.
   H.   Any violation shall be deemed an infraction as set forth in section
5-4-13 of this chapter. (Ord. 358, 1-8-2004)
5-4-11: CARE OF TREES WITHIN CITY:
   A.   City Responsibilities: The city shall be responsible for the following:
      1.   Care and maintenance of park trees and shrubs.
      2.   Removal of dead, diseased or hazardous park trees, limbs, and
shrubs.
      3.   Controlling insects and diseases of park trees and shrubs.
      4.   Managing insect and disease management programs for all trees in the
city.
   B.   Private Owner Responsibilities: Every owner shall be responsible for
the following:
      1.   Meeting all the requirements and obtaining all the permits necessary
for work done on adjacent public trees as described in this chapter.
      2.   Care and maintenance of public trees and shrubs located on the right
of way adjacent to the owner's private real property, including the following:
         a.   Removal and replacement of public trees or removal of those
portions of public trees declared to be a public nuisance when they are located
on the right of way adjacent to the owner's private real property.
         b.   Pruning of public trees and shrubs located on the right of way
adjacent to the owner's private real property. Branches of trees that overhang
sidewalks must be pruned to provide eight feet (8') of vertical clearance and
branches that overhang the street must be pruned to provide twelve feet (12')
of vertical clearance.
         c.   Control of injurious pests for public trees and limbs located on
the right of way adjacent to the owner's private real property.
         d.   Repairing damage done to the sidewalks and surrounding areas by
the roots of private trees or shrubs, or public trees and shrubs located on the
right of way adjacent to the owner's private real property.
         e.   Removal of private trees and shrubs located on the owner's
private real property that have been declared to be a public nuisance.
      3.   Control of significant pests for private trees and shrubs on the
owner's private property.
      4.   Removal of all tree or shrub work debris from the street and
sidewalk, by sunset of the day on which the work is done unless street closure
is authorized. (Ord. 358, 1-8-2004)
5-4-12: PUBLIC NUISANCES:
   A.   The following are hereby declared public nuisances under this chapter:
      1.   Any dead tree or shrub located on city owned property, including the
public right of way.
      2.   Any tree or shrub on public or private property that harbors
pathogens or injurious insects which reasonably may be expected to injure or
harm other trees or shrubs.
      3.   Any tree or shrub which obstructs the free passage of pedestrian or
vehicular traffic or which obstructs a streetlight or traffic control device.
      4.   Any tree or shrub, or portion thereby, which obstructs the view in
the "visibility triangle" as defined by Idaho Code.
      5.   Any tree or shrub which, by reason of location or condition,
constitutes an imminent danger to the health, safety or welfare of the general
public.
   B.   In the event any nuisance specified above shall be allowed to occur,
the city shall give notice of such nuisance to the property owner or person
occupying such premises. Such notice shall be delivered either by personal
service or by the mail of the same addressed to the property owner or occupant
of such premises and deposited postage prepaid in the United States mail. Such
notice shall be effective upon delivery if served personally or upon mailing if
delivered by mail. Such notice shall give ten (10) days from the date of
delivery or of mailing, as the case may be, within which the nuisance must be
abated.
   C.   If the nuisance shall not be abated by the time specified in the
notice, the allowance of the nuisance to continue is hereby deemed an
infraction. Each day of occurrence thereafter shall constitute a new offense.
(Ord. 358, 1-8-2004)
5-4-13: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any provision of this chapter is guilty of an
infraction and is subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 358, 1-8-2004)
CHAPTER 5
CEMETERY
SECTION:
5-5-1: City Cemetery Designated
5-5-2: Definitions
5-5-3: Establishment Of Regulations
5-5-3-1: Fees
5-5-4: Administration And Care
5-5-5: Records
5-5-6: Ownership
5-5-7: Compliance With Applicable Laws
5-5-8: Rights Of City Reserved
5-5-9: Sale Of Burial Spaces; Certificates Of Ownership
5-5-10: Installment Purchases
5-5-11: Rights Of Certificate Owners
5-5-12: Transfer Of Ownership
5-5-13: Buy Back
5-5-14: Authorization For Interment
5-5-15: Liability Of City; Interment
5-5-16: Interments
5-5-17: Burial Of Indigent Persons
5-5-18: Disinterments
5-5-19: Number Of Burials In Site
5-5-20: Monuments And Markers
5-5-21: Fences, Grade, And Maintenance Of Lots
5-5-22: Trees, Flowers, And Shrubs
5-5-23: Rules Of Conduct
5-5-24: Penalty For Violation
5-5-1: CITY CEMETERY DESIGNATED:
Evergreen cemetery, located at 833 Fairfield Road, has since its purchase in
1926 been designated as, and shall continue to be, a city cemetery. This
cemetery shall be maintained by the city for the burial of the human dead.
(Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
BLOCK: Portion of a cemetery which is usually defined by roads or other
boundaries around its perimeter and which is divided into lots and spaces.
BURIAL: The permanent disposition of human remains by burial, inurnment or
dispersal of cremains.
BURIAL RIGHT: The right to inter in a burial space; this is not title to land,
but merely a right to be buried in a described space.
BURIAL SPACE: A grave space, cremation garden space or niche, used or intended
to be used for the burial of human remains.
CEMETERY: A place of burial for earth interments, columbarium for cinerary
interments, or a combination of these.
CERTIFICATE OF OWNERSHIP: A written document issued by the city to a purchaser
of a grave space, which document evidences ownership of a right to be buried in
the specific grave space.
COLUMBARIUM: An aboveground structure containing niches for the inurnment of
cremated human remains.
CREMAINS: Cremated human remains.
CREMATION GARDEN: An outdoor area dedicated to the deposit of cremains.
FAMILY: Those persons related by blood, marriage or law, or descended from a
common ancestor.
FEES: City council establishes fees to be assessed for cemetery services.
GRAVE SPACE: A space of ground sufficient in size for burial of the remains of
one casket, as specified by the cemetery plat.
INTERMENT: The permanent disposition of human remains by burial, inurnment or
dispersal. (See definition of Burial.)
LOTS: A unit of purchase which may contain either one, four (4), or eight (8)
burial spaces as specified for the particular block.
MARKER: One piece stones which are customarily used to mark individual graves.
MEMORIAL: A generic term which includes a marker, monument, niche, plate or
other physical object used to identify the occupant of the grave space. A
memorial stone or plaque may also refer to a marker, monument or plaque
memorializing someone that is not actually interred in the lot.
MONUMENT: Memorials of more than one piece.
NEXT OF KIN: Relatives of a deceased person according to the Idaho laws of
intestacy. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-3: ESTABLISHMENT OF REGULATIONS:
The city council is authorized to establish regulations for the operation of
the city cemeteries, without limitation by enumeration; procedures concerning
interment, disinterment or removal; use of cemetery lots; charges for specific
services; provision of grave liners; standards for grave marking and fencing;
monument and marker restrictions; restrictions on planting flowers and shrubs;
and such other regulations as may be necessary for orderly and efficient
cemetery maintenance and improvement. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-3-1: FEES:
The city council shall establish fees for all grave spaces, opening and closing
graves, burial of ashes, disinterment and other related services provided by
the city. The city council may add, fix and change the charges from time to
time as necessary. All fees charged are to be paid to the city clerk prior to
the use of a grave for interment or other allowed activity or for any other
service being provided. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-4: ADMINISTRATION AND CARE:
The city cemeteries shall be managed and maintained by the city superintendent,
subject to budget and policy decisions made by the mayor and city council. All
grading, landscape work, improvements of any kind, care of burial spaces, all
burial space opening and closing, interments, disinterment, and removals shall
only be conducted under the supervision of the city superintendent. The city
superintendent is authorized to expend funds for cemetery activities as
appropriated in the city's annual budget. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-5: RECORDS:
The city clerk shall keep the official records of all cemetery plats,
certificates of ownership, certificate transfers, installment purchases,
consents to bury, permits, burials and any other related information. The city
clerk shall maintain a record of all sales of lots and receive all money for
the sale of lots, interment, and other services provided. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-6: OWNERSHIP:
The city retains full and complete control and management of the lands,
buildings, improvements, roads, walks, utilities, development, books, and
records of the cemeteries. The city also retains full and complete authority,
rights, and privileges to make, change, administer and enforce all cemetery
ordinances, rules, regulations, and restrictions. Purchase of a burial right in
the city cemetery does not transfer real estate title to the owner. (Ord. 367,
2-10-2005)
5-5-7: COMPLIANCE WITH APPLICABLE LAWS:
All interments, disinterments, and removals are subject to cemetery rules and
regulations, and all city, state, and federal laws, rules and regulations.
(Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-8: RIGHTS OF CITY RESERVED:
   A.   Improve: The city reserves the right to improve the cemetery.
Improvements may include enlarging, replatting, reducing, or changing the
boundaries, establishing columbaria, or other activity deemed necessary by the
city council for the betterment of the cemetery.
   B.   Designate Uses: The city reserves the right to designate appropriate
areas for columbaria, cremation gardens, mausoleums, and other aboveground
structures.
   C.   Install And Change Drainage: The city reserves the right to lay,
maintain, and operate, or to alter or change pipelines or ditches for
irrigation systems, drainage or any other watercourses in any part of the
cemetery.
   D.   Restore: The city reserves the right, at the city's sole option and
expense, to restore, repair, or reset any grave marker or memorial placed upon
any lot or grave space, to include any marble, granite, bronze, concrete, or
stone work in any section, or to repair or rebuild any damaged structure,
building or utility.
   E.   Dispose Of Buy Back Spaces: The city reserves the right to buy back
spaces in a manner best serving the interest of the cemetery.
   F.   Ingress And Egress: The city reserves a perpetual right to enter and to
leave over any burial space for passage to and from other spaces. This right
extends to those lawfully within the cemetery. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-9: SALE OF BURIAL SPACES; CERTIFICATES OF OWNERSHIP:
   A.   The city clerk shall keep accurate record of all burial spaces sold in
the city cemetery. The price for the right to use each type of burial space
shall be established by the city council.
   B.   The city clerk shall issue a certificate of ownership to the purchaser
of a right to use a burial space for the burial of human dead, which shall
contain the following information:
      1.   The name and address of the space owner, a description of the burial
space location and the purchase price paid.
      2.   A statement that the certificate of ownership represents only a
right to be buried in the described space and does not convey any interest or
title to the property upon which the space is located.
      3.   The signature of the mayor and city clerk. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-10: INSTALLMENT PURCHASES:
   A.   Purchasers of certificates of ownership of burial spaces may pay the
appropriate purchase price in installments.
   B.   The written installment purchase contract shall:
      1.   Not include interest.
      2.   Require, at the time of contract execution, cash payment of at least
ten percent (10%) of the purchase price which shall be deducted from the amount
to be paid in installments.
      3.   Limit the term not to extend over a period of more than twelve (12)
months.
      4.   Include an acknowledgement that failure to pay any installment
within six (6) months of the installment due date shall terminate the contract,
together with any legal interest the purchaser may have in the installment
contract or burial space. Installment payment made pursuant to a contract
terminated in accord with this section shall be forfeited to the city.
   C.   In the case of such failure to pay, the city shall give the purchaser
written notice of termination for failure to pay any installment within four
(4) months of the installment due date, allowing the purchaser sixty (60) days
to make payment before actual termination, sent to the purchaser's last known
address via first class U.S. mail.
   D.   The city clerk shall not issue any certificate or permit burial in any
space covered by an installment contract until the purchaser has fulfilled the
contractual obligations and paid the space purchase price in full. (Ord. 367,
2-10-2005)
5-5-11: RIGHTS OF CERTIFICATE OWNERS:
   A.   Interment: Any burial space conveyed by a certificate of ownership
shall be considered a grant of the right to burial or interment in the space
described on the certificate.
   B.   Consent To Bury: A certificate owner may consent to the burial of any
deceased person in the burial space described on the certificate. Consent for a
nonfamily member shall be given by the certificate owner in writing and
submitted to the city clerk. Consent to bury shall not act as a transfer of
ownership of the burial space.
   C.   Disinterment Or Removal: No disinterment or removal of remains interred
pursuant to a consent to bury shall be undertaken without permission of the
next of kin or legal representative of the deceased. In the event of
disinterment, the consent to bury shall be void and the interment or burial
rights shall revert to the certificate owner.
   D.   Right Of Descent: Upon the death of the certificate owner, any unused
burial spaces shall pass as provided in the owner's last will and testament.
Any unused burial spaces not effectively disposed of by the owner's last will
and testament shall pass to the owner's heirs as prescribed in the Idaho
probate code.
   E.   No Transfer Without Approval: No burial spaces shall be transferable,
except with the consent of the city in accord with this code.
   F.   Change Of Address: It shall be the duty of every burial space owner to
keep the city clerk fully informed of the owner's mailing address, and to
notify the city clerk of any changes. Written notice sent to any certificate
owner at the last registered address on file shall be considered sufficient and
proper legal notice. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-12: TRANSFER OF OWNERSHIP:
   A.   Authorized: The transfer of a certificate of the right to use a burial
space may be made with the consent of the city. All lots transferred shall be
subject to the rules and regulations now in force or which may hereinafter be
adopted, and shall be used for no purpose than for the burial of the human
dead.
   B.   Method: The transfer of a certificate of ownership of any burial space
may be made:
      1.   During the certificate owner's lifetime through the act of sale or
give to another party made in writing with the owner's full intent to
relinquish any right to occupy or use the burial space.
      2.   By the certificate owner's last will and testament; or
      3.   By the applicable laws of intestacy.
   C.   Approval: No transfer of a certificate of ownership shall be effective
until approved by the city. Prior to approval, the city clerk shall require the
following:
      1.   The original certificate of ownership.
      2.   The bill of sale or other documentation transferring the right for
burial.
      3.   Any other information required by the cemetery rules and
regulations.
      4.   Payment of any indebtedness or installment payment due on the burial
space.
   D.   City Approval: The city shall give approval by issuing a new
certificate of ownership to the party of transference and shall record the
transfer in the cemetery records. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-13: BUY BACK:
   A.   The city may repurchase or buy back any certificate of ownership for
any unused or unoccupied burial space under the following conditions:
      1.   Ownership of the burial space is clear and evidenced by a valid
certificate of ownership;
      2.   The city verifies:
         a.   The space is unused and unoccupied;
         b.   No markers or monuments are erected on the space;
         c.   Sufficient funds for buy back are budgeted and appropriated; and
      3.   The certificate owner completes a buy back application.
   B.   If the burial space is eligible for buy back, the city clerk may pay
the certificate owner one-half (1/2) of the current burial space purchase
price. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-14: AUTHORIZATION FOR INTERMENT:
   A.   The city reserves the right to refuse burial in any burial space unless
the city receives proper authorization by the burial space owner of record.
   B.   The city reserves the right to make an interment of any member of the
immediate family of the burial space owner upon authorization by a member of
the immediate family of the burial space owner.
   C.   The city will accept authorization for interment through a funeral
home.
   D.   The burial space owner may consent to the burial of any deceased person
by giving written authorization to the city clerk for said interment.
   E.   The city may permit telephone authorization for immediate burial.
However, the city shall not be held responsible for any order given by
telephone, or for any mistake occurring from the want of precise and proper
telephonic instructions as to the particular space, size and location of a
burial space where interment is desired. Any changes, adjustments, or
correction necessitated by mistakes shall be at the expense of the burial space
owner or owner's agent. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-15: LIABILITY OF CITY; INTERMENT:
   A.   Delay From Protest: The city shall in no way be liable for any delay in
interment of a body where a protest to the interment has been made or where the
cemetery rules and regulations have been violated. The city shall be under no
duty to recognize any protest of interment.
   B.   Not Responsible For Identity: The city shall not be liable for the
truth or correctness of the information contained in the interment permit, nor
for the identity of the person sought to be interred or disinterred.
   C.   Errors May Be Corrected: The city shall not be liable for and reserves
the right to correct any errors that may have been made by it. Correction may
include substitution of a similar burial space.
   D.   Location Of Interment Space: When the instructions regarding the
location of a burial space cannot be opened where specified, the city shall
contact the funeral home, agent or family to make suitable arrangements. The
city shall not be liable in damages for any error made.
   E.   Removal: The city shall exercise the utmost care in making a removal,
but it shall assume no liability for damage incurred to any casket or burial
case or urn in making the removal. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-16: INTERMENTS:
   A.   No interment will be permitted, nor shall any body be received for
burial, unless a proper certificate and burial transit permit for the deceased
is received by the city.
   B.   A minimum of forty eight (48) hours' notice is required to be given to
the city before any interment. Such notice shall comply with the authorization
for interment and shall include the size of the case used and the location of
the grave. Less notice may be permitted in the case of a health related
emergency.
   C.   Only one interment of a casket shall be made in a single grave. The
addition of one cremain in a grave with a casket is permissible. Two (2)
cremains may be interred in one grave. Other arrangements may be granted by the
city.
   D.   The city will endeavor to conduct interments on the date and at the
time requested by the family. The city reserves the right to refuse
unreasonable requests.
   E.   The city will endeavor to accommodate graveside services. An alternate
area may be made available due to weather constraints or any safety concern.
   F.   Burial vaults shall be required for all burials at the city cemetery.
Vaults made of heavy noncorrosive metal, fiberglass or other materials which
meet or exceed the performance standards and specifications of concrete liners
will be permitted. All cremains are to be placed in a nonperishable container
prior to interment in the ground.
   G.   All graves must be opened and closed by the city, and will be subjected
to the charges as described herein, which shall be paid in advance to the city
clerk. Special permission may be granted to allow family members to hand dig a
grave and/or perform closing by hand. Such activity shall be under the
supervision of the city and will still be subject to charges. (Ord. 367, 2-10-
2005)
5-5-17: BURIAL OF INDIGENT PERSONS:
The city council may from time to time designate lots to be reserved for the
burial of indigent persons. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-18: DISINTERMENTS:
   A.   Disinterments shall only be conducted during normal work hours and on
regularly scheduled workdays.
   B.   Before disinterment or removal, each of the following shall be provided
by the city clerk:
      1.   Submittal of a death certificate by the next of kin or legal
representative of the deceased.
      2.   Submittal of the name of the funeral home and director conducting
the initial burial.
      3.   Submittal of court order, if appropriate.
      4.   If the body or cremains are to be moved out of the cemetery to
another location, submittal of an authorization permit from the state, by the
next of kin, legal representative of the deceased or the funeral home.
   C.   The city reserves the right to verify all documents submitted for a
disinterment, to refuse to conduct a disinterment if the necessary forms and
information are not submitted, and to refuse to permit or conduct a
disinterment if removal would present a health hazard to cemetery staff or the
public. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-19: NUMBER OF BURIALS IN SITE:
There will be allowed one casket burial, or two (2) cremains burials, or one
casket and one cremains urn burial in one grave space. Other arrangements may
be granted by the city. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-20: MONUMENTS AND MARKERS:
   A.   No person owning a burial right in the city cemetery or any person or
firm selling markers to persons owning lots in the city cemetery shall set any
monument or marker of any kind without the permission of the city. The city
shall approve the location of any monument or marker prior to being set.
Requests to locate graves and/or to mark or approve locations for monuments or
markers should be made at least twenty four (24) hours in advance.
   B.   All monuments and gravestones shall be placed upon foundations built of
solid masonry, which shall not be less in size than the lower base of the
structure, and which shall be of sufficient depth, in the opinion of the city
superintendent, to support the monument. There shall be constructed a collar of
concrete four inches (4") wide around the base at the bottom of each monument,
or granite may be used as the foundation for the gravestone and must also have
a four inch (4") wide collar around the base of the monument. The monument must
be glued and doweled securely to the granite. The top of the concrete collar or
granite collar must be flush with the surrounding ground level.
   C.   All stones of sufficient thickness to stand alone shall be properly
doweled or secured to their base. The base of all monuments shall be cut so as
to set fairly level on foundations.
   D.   All monuments and markers shall not encroach upon the alleys, street,
or walkways, nor shall they encroach upon any adjoining grave space.
   E.   The city shall not be liable for any damage or injury to raised
letterings, carving, or ornaments on any memorial or other structure on any
lot.
   F.   Memorial stones or plaques, memorializing someone that is not actually
interred in the lot, may be added to a grave space.
   G.   The number of monuments, stones, or markers shall be limited to two (2)
per gravesite. Special permission may be granted by the city on a case by case
basis for one additional marker or stone beyond that number. (Ord. 367, 2-10-
2005)
5-5-21: FENCES, GRADE, AND MAINTENANCE OF LOTS:
   A.   No enclosure of any nature, such as fences, copings, hedges, or
ditches, shall be allowed upon or around any plots, lots, or blocks without
prior approval from the city.
   B.   No bricks, rocks, or other materials shall be allowed to cover any
plots, lots, or block without prior approval from the city.
   C.   The city may mark individual lots or blocks by an iron pin or pipe at
each corner set level with the ground.
   D.   The grade of all lots shall be determined by city. Grave mounds shall
not be permitted, nor shall lots be raised above the established grade.
   E.   The graves shall receive the same general care as other parts of the
lawn. The grass is to be cut and leaves and debris raked off at the same time
that the remainder of the lawn is cleaned. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-22: TREES, FLOWERS, AND SHRUBS:
   A.   No trees, shrubs, or plants shall be planted, pruned, or removed
without the consent of the city. The city shall have full authority to prune,
remove, or transplant any trees, shrubs, or plants when it is considered for
the best interest of the cemetery, or it is advisable to do so. No trees shall
be removed from the city cemetery without specific approval of the city
council.
   B.   Pot hangers should be placed next to the collar of the headstone.
Flowers and other items left on a grave shall not interfere with the
maintenance of the cemetery.
   C.   The city is not liable for the safety of any flower or other item left
on a grave, and reserves the right to remove dead flowers, broken vases, and
other items in a broken or deteriorated state. Items interfering with the
maintenance of the cemetery may also be removed by the city. (Ord. 367, 2-10-
2005)
5-5-23: RULES OF CONDUCT:
   A.   All persons are prohibited from gathering or taking away any flowers,
wild or cultivated, or breaking, damaging, or destroying any shrub, plant, or
tree upon the cemetery grounds.
   B.   All persons are prohibited from writing upon, or in any manner marring,
defacing, or injuring any monument in the cemetery; from injuring, defacing, or
removing from any grave any monument, marker, ornament, or any other property;
from cutting, disfiguring, or injuring the fence, gate or other enclosures
around or within the cemetery.
   C.   All persons are prohibited from playing any games, disturbing the
quiet, peace, and good order of the cemetery by loud noise or improper conduct,
or any other activities unrelated to the proper use, good order, and decorum of
the cemetery.
   D.   Driving on lots, backing over graves, cutting corners, or speeding in
the cemetery is prohibited.
   E.   It shall be unlawful for any person to dig, or attempt to dig, any
grave in the cemetery, or exhume, or remove any corpse from any grave therein
without the permission of the city. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
5-5-24: PENALTY FOR VIOLATION:
Any person who violates any provision of this chapter is guilty of an
infraction, and is subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 367, 2-10-2005)
CHAPTER 6
STREET APPROACHES
SECTION:
5-6-1: Permit Required
5-6-2: Definitions
5-6-3: General Rules For Approaches
5-6-4: Application For Permit
5-6-5: Traffic Study Requirements
5-6-6: Fees
5-6-7: Deposit
5-6-8: Issuance Of Permit
5-6-9: Appeal
5-6-10: Substandard Approaches
5-6-11: Unapproved Approaches
5-6-12: Inspection
5-6-13: Final Approval
5-6-14: Maintenance Responsibility
5-6-15: Penalty
5-6-1: PERMIT REQUIRED:
No work of any nature shall be performed on public right of way until an
approved permit has been issued, including the construction of temporary or
permanent approaches, and the revision of or addition to existing approaches.
(Ord. 391, 9-25-2008)
5-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
APPLICANT: Any person, persons, corporation, partnership, or other singular or
plural individuals making application for an approach.
APPROACH: The section of the public right of way between the outside edge of
the roadway shoulder and the public right of way line which is designed as an
approved roadway for the movement of vehicles between the public roadway and
the abutting property.
CONSTRUCTION PERMIT: The authorization issued to an applicant to construct an
approach.
HIGHWAY: The entire width between the boundary lines of every way publicly
maintained when any part is open to the use of the public for vehicular travel,
with jurisdiction extending to the adjacent property line, including sidewalks,
shoulders, berms, and rights of way not intended for motorized traffic. The
terms "public street" and "public right of way" are interchangeable with
highway.
FINAL PERMIT: The formal approval of an approach issued to the permittee.
PERMITTEE: The person, persons, corporation, partnership, or other singular or
plural individuals approved for an approach through the application process.
PRIVATE APPROACH: An approach used for access to a private residential
property.
PUBLIC APPROACH: An approach used by the public for access to a public,
commercial or industrial facility.
PUBLIC RIGHT OF WAY: A right of way open to the public and under the city's
jurisdiction, where the city has no obligation to construct or maintain said
right of way for vehicular traffic. A term used to define a specific space.
ROADSIDE: A general term denoting the area adjoining the outer edge of the
shoulder.
ROADWAY: That portion of a highway improved, designed or ordinarily used for
vehicular travel, exclusive of sidewalks, shoulders, berms and right of way.
STREET: See definition of Highway.
TEMPORARY APPROACH: An approach which is permitted for a specified time not to
exceed a six (6) month period. Temporary approaches require a permit.
TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES: A collective term for barricades, cones, signs,
flagging personnel and other items used to stop, direct, or change the flow of
traffic for a temporary period of time. Traffic control devices are used to
accommodate the safety of vehicles, pedestrians and workers.
TRAVELED WAY: The portion of the roadway for the movement of vehicles. (Ord.
391, 9-25-2008)
5-6-3: GENERAL RULES FOR APPROACHES:
   A.   Approaches shall be for the bona fide purpose of securing access.
   B.   The location, design, construction, and operation of all approaches
shall comply with the design principles and geometric restrictions established
in the "City Of Plummer Approach Manual" as adopted by the city council. The
approach should be designed for the actual and future property access
requirements. Approaches shall not interfere with the drainage of the roadway.
   C.   The city reserves the right to require the permittee, its successors or
assigns, to make any changes, additions, repairs or relocations to any approach
or its appurtenances within the public right of way for necessary relocation,
reconstruction, or widening of the highway and/or to provide proper protection
of life and property on, or adjacent to, the roadway.
   D.   Generally, no part of the public right of way shall be used for:
      1.   The parking of vehicles except in authorized parking areas.
      2.   The servicing, refueling, repairing of vehicles except for
emergencies.
      3.   Displays, sales, exhibits, business signs, etc.
   E.   The safe, efficient passage and protection of vehicles and pedestrians
during any work within public right of way covered by permit is very important
and shall be the responsibility of the permittee. Barricades, signs and other
traffic control devices shall be erected and maintained by the permittee in
conformance with the current "Manual On Uniform Traffic Control Devices" during
any work within public right of way.
   F.   Permittee shall furnish all material, labor and equipment involved in
the construction of the approach. This shall include furnishing drainage pipe
and other requirements that may be specified on the permit. Materials and
workmanship shall be in good quality and are subject to inspection and
approval. (Ord. 391, 9-25-2008)
5-6-4: APPLICATION FOR PERMIT:
   A.   Application for an approach permit shall be made on the form provided
by the city clerk's office and shall be signed by the owner of the abutting
real property or his authorized representative.
   B.   The application form shall be accompanied by a sketch showing the
location of the highway, existing and proposed approach changes, location of
other proposed work to be done within the public right of way, highway signs in
the area of the approach, and a list of all materials to be used. The cost of
relocating any highway signs shall be borne by the permittee.
   C.   Applications for temporary approaches shall also include a statement
explaining how the applicant proposes to remove the approach and restore the
right of way.
   D.   Permit applications for approaches which will generate over fifty (50)
cars per hour during the peak hour, may be required by the city council to
include a traffic impact study. (Ord. 391, 9-25-2008)
5-6-5: TRAFFIC STUDY REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Proposed approaches, generating over fifty (50) cars per hour during
the peak hour, may be required by the city council to include a traffic impact
study with the application. All costs of said study shall be borne by the
applicant.
   B.   The study shall include data on the following:
      1.   Existing peak hour traffic volumes and conditions.
      2.   Directional distribution estimates of added traffic.
      3.   Projections of added traffic volumes for all appropriate critical
hours.
      4.   Determination of needed improvements, traffic controls, approach
locations and their design and the impact on nearby traffic control.
      5.   Identification of any additional highway right of way which might be
required.
   C.   The results of the impact study should enable the city council to:
      1.   Verify the need for capacity improvements along access streets and
critical intersections.
      2.   Consider the effects on the local transportation system.
      3.   Enable the city to check access design.
      4.   Determine a fair and equitable means of cost sharing between the
developer and the city for needed intersection or access improvements,
including added traffic lanes and traffic control devices. (Ord. 391, 9-25-
2008)
5-6-6: FEES:
   A.   A nonrefundable application fee for the issuance and inspection of an
approach permit shall be set by the city council and may be changed from time
to time. A fee schedule shall be set for new approach permits, temporary
approach permits, alteration or improvement permits for existing approaches,
and for special traffic study reviews.
   B.   Application fees will be waived for improvement permits when the
approach width is changed on an approach which is already constructed to
standards, provided that safety and drainage are not adversely affected. (Ord.
391, 9-25-2008)
5-6-7: DEPOSIT:
   A.   A deposit will be required for all new approaches. Said deposit shall
be returned to applicant if proper construction is completed within one hundred
eighty (180) days of the issuance of the construction permit.
   B.   In the case of a temporary approach, the deposit shall be returned
after the approach has been removed, inspected and the restoration of the right
of way approved within one hundred eighty (180) days of the issuance of the
construction permit.
   C.   The deposit is considered to be forfeited in full if the permittee has
not complied with the construction permit and received a final permit within
the time allowed. No interest shall be paid on deposits. (Ord. 391, 9-25-2008)
5-6-8: ISSUANCE OF PERMIT:
   A.   Construction permits shall not be issued for permanent or temporary
approaches until a complete application is received with the appropriate fee
and deposit. Permits shall be issued by the city clerk's office.
   B.   Final approach approval shall be issued only after final inspection and
approval of the superintendent of public works. (Ord. 391, 9-25-2008)
5-6-9: APPEAL:
   A.   Any applicant who has made application for a permit under the
provisions of this chapter and who has been denied a construction permit or
final approach permit, or had a permit revoked shall have the right to an
appeal before the Plummer city council by filing a written appeal with the city
clerk within fifteen (15) days following the date of the action or decision
giving rise to the appeal.
   B.   The hearing on this matter shall be held before the city council of the
city at its next available special or regularly scheduled meeting. (Ord. 391,
9-25-2008)
5-6-10: SUBSTANDARD APPROACHES:
   A.   If a substandard approach is constructed, the permittee shall be given
notice to upgrade the approach to the prescribed standards on the permit or
have a plan of action approved by the superintendent of public works with a
completion date.
   B.   Notice of a substandard approach shall be provided by posting the right
of way with the substandard approach and a copy mailed to the landowner of
record by U.S. postal mail. Such notice shall provide ten (10) days to take
corrective measures unless a hazardous situation is created by the permittee or
party and immediate corrective work is ordered by the city.
   C.   Permits shall be revoked for approaches which are not upgraded to the
prescribed standards and action taken to remove the approaches. (Ord. 391, 9-
25-2008)
5-6-11: UNAPPROVED APPROACHES:
   A.   Approaches under construction without an approved construction permit
shall be given notice to stop work immediately and obtain the proper permit.
   B.   Notice of a substandard or unapproved approach shall be provided by
posting the right of way with the substandard or unapproved approach and a copy
mailed to the landowner of record by U.S. postal mail. Such notice shall
provide ten (10) days to take corrective measures unless a hazardous situation
is created by the permittee or party and immediate corrective work is ordered
by the city.
   C.   Unapproved approaches shall be removed by the city at the end of that
time and legal action initiated to collect the removal cost. (Ord. 391, 9-25-
2008)
5-6-12: INSPECTION:
Approaches are subject to inspection during and after the construction of an
approach. Inspections shall be performed by authorized city personnel. (Ord.
391, 9-25-2008)
5-6-13: FINAL APPROVAL:
Approaches which have been completed to the city's standards and passed
inspection shall receive final approval issued to the permittee. (Ord. 391, 9-
25-2008)
5-6-14: MAINTENANCE RESPONSIBILITY:
Once the approach has been constructed and approved, the city will maintain the
drainage including ditches and culverts that may have been required. The
permittee is responsible for the general maintenance of the approach including
surfacing, gravel, snow removal, etc., to allow their use of the approach.
(Ord. 391, 9-25-2008)
5-6-15: PENALTY:
Any person violating any of the sections or provisions of this chapter shall be
deemed guilty of an infraction and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject
to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 391, 9-25-2008)
CHAPTER 7
PARADE REGULATIONS
SECTION:
5-7-1: Purpose
5-7-2: Definitions
5-7-3: Permit Required
5-7-4: Parade Requirements And Restrictions
5-7-5: Exemptions
5-7-6: Permit Application
5-7-7: Contents Of Permit Application
5-7-8: Application Fee
5-7-9: Denial
5-7-10: Revocation
5-7-11: Appeal Procedure
5-7-12: Interference Prohibited
5-7-13: Penalties
5-7-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of these regulations is to set forth the standards of issuance for
a parade permit. It is further the purpose of these regulations to:
   A.   Assure that emergency services such as police, fire, and ambulance
services are available for a parade taking place within the city.
   B.   Assure that emergency services such as police, fire, and ambulance
services are not unreasonably inhibited in their ability to travel on and to
cross public streets used by parades.
   C.   Assure that private business activities are not unreasonably impacted
by parades.
   D.   Assure that traffic on public streets is not unreasonably disturbed or
disrupted by parades.
   E.   Assure that public safety can be maintained.
   F.   Assure that public property can be protected from harm. (Ord. 389, 5-8-
2008)
5-7-2: DEFINITIONS:
APPLICANT: Any person applying for a "permit" as defined herein. The true
applicant for any such permit shall be the sponsoring entity whether such
sponsoring entity is an individual person, corporation, a partnership or other
legal entity of any type.
PARADE: Any march, marathon, procession, or like activity consisting of people,
animals, or vehicles, or any combination thereof, within the city with the
intent of attracting public attention or achieving some other expressive
purpose which might interfere with, or has the potential to interfere with, the
normal flow or regulation of traffic upon the streets.
PERMIT: The permit as required by this chapter for a "parade" as defined
herein. An approved application will serve as a permit. (Ord. 389, 5-8-2008)
5-7-3: PERMIT REQUIRED:
No person shall engage in, participate in, or conduct any "parade" as defined
in this chapter unless a permit has been issued by the city clerk for the date
and location involved. (Ord. 389, 5-8-2008)
5-7-4: PARADE REQUIREMENTS AND RESTRICTIONS:
The following prohibitions and regulations shall apply to activities requiring
a permit:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person in charge of, or responsible for
the conduct of, a duly permitted activity requiring a permit to knowingly fail
to comply with any condition of the permit.
   B.   No permit shall be issued for a parade to commence before seven o'clock
(7:00) A.M. All parades shall terminate prior to eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M.
   C.   No parade requiring a permit shall exceed two (2) hours in length.
   D.   All parade participants shall assemble for the parade at the time and
location designated in the parade permit and shall disperse from public
property after the conclusion of the parade in order that regular traffic
patterns might be restored.
   E.   Parade organizers shall assure to the satisfaction of the chief of
police that they do not intend to engage in violence or other unlawful conduct
and do not intend to incite others to do so.
   F.   Only one parade permit will be granted for the same calendar day unless
absolute assurance can be provided that the permitted events will not conflict
and that public service obligations will not exceed the fiscal and operational
limits of city personnel. If two (2) or more permit applications are filed for
the same date, the application which is first accepted shall have priority for
a permit.
   G.   The permit may limit or condition the number of participants, the
length of the event, the time and location of the event, or the manner of the
event where necessary to prevent violence, to avoid serious inconvenience to
those needing access to commercial or public services, to avoid interference
with the movement of police or other emergency vehicles where such limitations
or conditions provide ample opportunity for exercise of constitutionally
protected rights.
   H.   There shall be no discrimination in granting, denying, or conditionally
granting permits under this chapter based upon statutorily protected or
constitutionally guaranteed individual rights.
   I.   If the parade is to be held, either in part or in its entirety, upon
Highways 5 or 95, or either of them, a state permit must be obtained and a copy
of the permit provided to the Plummer city clerk not later than forty eight
(48) hours prior to the scheduled beginning of the parade. Any permit issued by
the city shall not be effective until the clerk has received a copy of the
state permit. (Ord. 389, 5-8-2008)
5-7-5: EXEMPTIONS:
The following shall be exempt from obtaining a parade permit:
   A.   Funeral processions.
   B.   City sponsored parades.
   C.   Military parades of an immediate celebratory nature.
   D.   Unanticipated events as approved by the city council on a case by case
basis. (Ord. 389, 5-8-2008)
5-7-6: PERMIT APPLICATION:
   A.   The completed application form must be received by the city clerk with
the appropriate fee at least sixty (60) days prior to the date of the parade.
The time frame set forth herein may be waived in the discretion of the city
council upon a finding that such a waiver would not compromise the ability of
the city to prepare for the activity for which the permit is requested. No
application shall be deemed received until such time as the entire application
and all of the information required therein shall have been delivered to the
city clerk.
   B.   Prior to issuance of the permit, the chief of police must determine
from the information contained in the application, information developed from
other sources, and knowledge of the police department that:
      1.   The route, timing and nature of the parade will not substantially
interrupt the safe and orderly movement of traffic contiguous to its route or
elsewhere in the community.
      2.   The route, timing and nature of the parade will not require more
police officers than can reasonably be provided, while still providing normal
protection to the city.
      3.   The route, timing and nature of the parade will not unduly interfere
with the proper fire, ambulance, police or other public services to areas
contiguous to the parade or elsewhere in the community.
      4.   The parade is not likely to cause injury to persons or property or
to create disorderly conduct or create a disturbance. If the chief of police is
unable to conclude this, he shall meet and confer with the applicant to
determine what steps, if any, the applicant could take to avoid disorder or to
minimize the possibility of a public disturbance.
      5.   The person seeking the issuance of a parade permit has agreed to
furnish qualified road guards as needed to assist the police department or has
provided evidence of contractual arrangement to provide the same. (Ord. 389, 5-
8-2008)
5-7-7: CONTENTS OF PERMIT APPLICATION:
Each permit application shall state at least the following, and the applicant
shall adhere to and be bound by any commitments made in an application
submittal:
   A.   The full name, street address, mailing address, telephone number, e-
mail address, and facsimile number, if any, of the person or organization
sponsoring the parade.
   B.   The name, mailing address, telephone number, e-mail address, and
facsimile number, if any, of the person in charge of the parade.
   C.   The date when the parade is to be conducted.
   D.   The name of the parade, if any.
   E.   The time the parade will begin to form, and the time the parade will
begin movement.
   F.   The place the parade will form, the route on the parade, and the place
the parade will disband along with the attachment of a map showing these
locations.
   G.   The approximate number of participants.
   H.   A documented plan for controlling disorderly or violent conduct if such
might reasonably be expected, a plan for maintaining traffic flow to commercial
and other establishments, a plan for sanitary and medical facilities, and for
cleanup.
   I.   A certificate of liability insurance for the event shall be attached to
the application showing the city as an additional insured, and evidencing that
the applicant has liability insurance in the amount of five hundred thousand
dollars ($500,000.00) for any damages to persons or property caused as a result
of the event.
   J.   Any other information required by the city clerk or chief of police to
enable them to understand the impacts of the proposed parade shall be provided.
   K.   A statement that the applicant shall comply with all permit conditions
and with all federal, state and local laws. (Ord. 389, 5-8-2008)
5-7-8: APPLICATION FEE:
   A.   A nonrefundable application fee to cover the expenses incident to
processing the application for the parade permit shall be paid to the city
clerk at the time of filing the application.
   B.   The parade application fee shall be such as may be prescribed from time
to time by the city council. (Ord. 389, 5-8-2008)
5-7-9: DENIAL:
   A.   A permit may be denied if:
      1.   The applicant has made on prior occasions material
misrepresentations regarding the nature or scope of a parade; or
      2.   The applicant has violated the terms of prior permits issued to or
on behalf of the applicant; or
      3.   The applicant has on prior occasions damaged city property and not
paid in full for such damages; or
      4.   There is clear and convincing evidence that the applicant, not
opponents of the applicant, intends to engage in violence or disorderly
conduct; or
      5.   The application is not complete with all required attachments and
fees.
   B.   In the event of denial, the reasons will be provided in writing and the
applicant notified that an appeal may be brought before the city council as set
forth below. (Ord. 389, 5-8-2008)
5-7-10: REVOCATION:
   A.   A previously approved permit may be revoked if:
      1.   It is found that the applicant has made material misrepresentations
regarding the nature or scope of a parade; or
      2.   There is clear and convincing evidence that the applicant, not
opponents of the applicant, intends to engage in violence or disorderly
conduct.
   B.   Any such cancellation shall be communicated to the applicant as soon as
possible after such determination has been made.
   C.   In the event an emergency occurs in relation to weather conditions,
civil disturbances or any other condition that imperils persons or property in
the area of the parade route, the city may revoke a permit previously granted.
In such case, the city shall give the applicant an opportunity to reschedule
the parade for a time when such emergency no longer exists. (Ord. 389, 5-8-
2008)
5-7-11: APPEAL PROCEDURE:
   A.   Any applicant shall have the right to appeal the denial of a permit or
imposition of conditions to the city council. The denied applicant must make
any appeal within seven (7) business days after transmittal of the denial or
conditional approval from the city clerk by filing written notice of appeal
with the city clerk setting out the reasons therefor in writing.
   B.   The city council will hear the appeal at a regular or special meeting
and reach a determination prior to the planned date and time of the parade.
Such decision shall be final and shall be communicated to the applicant in
writing. (Ord. 389, 5-8-2008)
5-7-12: INTERFERENCE PROHIBITED:
   A.   No person shall knowingly join in or participate in any parade without
the consent of the permit applicant, nor over his objections.
   B.   No person shall in any manner interfere with the progress or orderly
conduct of a permitted parade. (Ord. 389, 5-8-2008)
5-7-13: PENALTIES:
Any person found to be in violation of any provision of this chapter shall be
guilty of an infraction and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to
penalties provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 389, 5-8-2008)
CHAPTER 8
ROAD NAMES AND ADDRESSES
SECTION:
5-8-1: General Provisions
5-8-2: Implementation And Responsibilities
5-8-3: Performance Standards
5-8-4: Signing
5-8-5: Enforcement
5-8-1: GENERAL PROVISIONS:
   A.   Authority: This chapter is authorized under the provisions of Idaho
constitution article 12, section 2, and by Idaho Code title 50, chapter 13, and
title 67, chapter 65, as amended or subsequently codified.
   B.   Purpose: This chapter further implements portions of the City of
Plummer comprehensive plan and supplements the City of Plummer ordinances. Its
purpose is to provide the residents of the City of Plummer with a uniform and
standardized system of road naming and addressing to:
      1.   Minimize future road name and addressing conflicts.
      2.   Provide a database for city and county records and enhanced 911
service.
      3.   Expedite property identification by emergency services.
      4.   Comply with addressing guidelines issued by the National Emergency
Number Association (NENA), the U.S Postal Service (USPS), and emergency
communication providers.
   C.   Applicability: This chapter shall apply to all property and to all
public and private roads in the City of Plummer. (Ord. 474, 12-19-2024)
5-8-2: IMPLEMENTATION AND RESPONSIBILITIES:
   A.   The city code administrator shall have the responsibility of
implementing, enforcing and maintaining the addressing and road naming
standards as defined by this chapter.
   B.   Property owners are responsible for placing alphanumeric identification
and for erecting private road signs in accordance with the detailed performance
standards in section
5-8-4  of this chapter. Posting of addresses and road names must be done within
a six (6) month time frame after effective date hereof and all new developments
shall be issued addresses at the time of permit approval.
   C.   In the event that violations of this chapter are not connected by the
date required herein, the city may perform the work and bill the property owner
for work completed. (Ord. 474, 12-19-2024)
5-8-3: PERFORMANCE STANDARDS:
   A.   Road Designations: Designation of roads within the City of Plummer
shall be in accordance with the following guidelines, except in the case of
existing and recorded road designations:
      1.   All named roads that extend from incorporated areas into
unincorporated areas shall retain the same name except in the case of
duplication or noncompliance with this chapter.
      2.   Roads which have a definite north-south directional course shall be
designated as a "street". Roads which have a definite east-west directional
course shall be designated an "avenue".
      3.   Roads which do not have a definite directional course shall be
designated as a "road", "drive", "trail", "way" or "lane".
      4.   A dead end road or cul-de-sac less than one thousand feet (1,000')
in length, when not an extension of an existing road or a continuation of a
proposed road, shall be called a "court".
      5.   A road that has its ingress and egress on the same road shall be
designated a "loop".
      6.   A road that circles back upon itself shall be designated as a
"circle".
      7.   Special scenic routes or park drives may be designated "parkway".
      8.   A newly established road, which has less than a one hundred twenty
five foot (125') centerline alignment offset from an existing road, shall
continue the same road name. A newly established road, which has more than a
one hundred twenty five foot (125') centerline alignment offset from an
existing road, shall adopt a new name.
      9.   Duplicate road names are prohibited. Existing duplicated names shall
be corrected in accordance with these performance standards.
      10.   Both "L" shaped and "T" shaped streets or private roads should
carry the same name if either leg is one hundred feet (100') or less in length.
"L" shaped and "T" shaped streets or private roads over 100 feet in length each
should carry a different name on each leg of the "L" or the "T".
      11.   When a road name within the incorporated area of the City of
Plummer is duplicated by a road name within the county and such duplication
causes conflict, the City of Plummer and the county should work together to
decide which road should be renamed. Roads shall be renamed in accordance with
the procedures outlined in this chapter.
   B.   Addressing Along Roads:
      1.   Address numbers will run consecutively to the north, south, east and
west from the point of beginning.
      2.   From the point of beginning, one thousand six hundred (1,600)
address numbers will be added as each section line is crossed (approximately
1,600 per mile).
      3.   All addresses shall be defined with a direction letter (N, S, E, W)
following the address number.
      4.   Even numbers shall appear on the south and east side of roads, and
odd numbers on the north and west sides.
      5.   If a building or mobile home park has a number of entrances each
serving a separate occupant(s), then each entrance shall be assigned an
address. If whole numbers are exhausted, half numbers shall be utilized.
      6.   Mobile home parks and multi-family dwelling structures with one main
entrance shall be assigned one number with the owner of the park or structure
responsible for the individual numbering of each unit. Addressing of the
individual apartments or mobile homes within the structure shall be based upon
the postal addressing standards, publication 28, dated October 2023.
      7.   Circle and loop road direction designations shall be determined by
the road's predominate direction. Numbering shall start either at its north
intersection point with a north-south primary road, or at its west intersection
point with an east-west primary road and shall continue, according to the grid,
in a clockwise direction, as if the road were straight.
      8.   Properties with structure(s) which are accessed by a driveway shall
be assigned an address at the point where the driveway intersects a road.
      9.   If three (3) or more properties use one road as access, it shall be
assigned a road name and the structures shall be addressed in accordance with
these standards.
      10.   Properties accessed by a common right of way or easement with two
(2) or fewer living units or business structures shall be assigned an address
at the point where the right of way or easement intersects a public or private
road.
   C.   Road Naming Policy: "Roads" are defined as all vehicle paths of travel
serving three (3) or more properties, residences or businesses. Driveways or
other vehicle paths of travel serving less than three (3) properties,
residences or businesses shall not be named, to reduce administrative costs and
potential confusion for emergency service providers. In selecting road names,
consideration shall be given to the following:
      1.   Centerline alignment road name standards of subsection A8 of this
section shall be observed for noncontinuous roads, unless there is no
possibility for extension of the road to make it a continuous through road.
      2.   There shall be no duplication of existing names. Benewah County
shall assemble, update and maintain an official list of all road names
throughout the county for use by all jurisdictions.
      3.   Names of similar pronunciation and/or spelling shall be prohibited
(example: Briar Lane, Brier Lane).
      4.   Variations of the same name with a different road designation shall
be prohibited within the first word of the two (2) word title or in the road
extension (example: Pine Road, Pine Drive, Pine Lane).
      5.   No road name shall consist of more than two (2) words or contain
more than fourteen (14) letters, excluding the road direction (N, S, E, W) and
extension (street, lane, court, etc.).
      6.   No road shall have more than one name.
      7.   No road name shall contain the words north, south, east or west, or
any combination thereof, within the road name.
   D.   Naming Of New Roads Or Naming Of Existing Unnamed Roads: Any new road
to be established within the City of Plummer, public or private, or any
existing unnamed road, public or private, shall require a road name approved by
the mayor and city council.
      1.   In the case of plats, road names shall be specified on the final
plat map.
      2.   In the case of other new roads or naming of unnamed roads, the mayor
and city council will assign a road name in accordance with these standards.
Recommendations made by residents of the road and community at large may be
given considerable weight.
   E.   Renaming Of Existing Duplicated Road Names: Where duplicate names
exist, roads shall be immediately renamed by the mayor and city council to
eliminate the duplication. The mayor and city council will decide which roads
shall be renamed with consideration to the following criteria:
      1.   When the road was originally named.
      2.   The number of improved properties served by the road.
      3.   Other factors as deemed appropriate by the city council. When a road
name is duplicated by a road outside the city, the city shall work with the
county to decide which road shall be renamed.
      4.   Whether the road contains the name or is referencing a figure or
individual of importance to the City of Plummer.
   F.   Renaming Of Roads: In cases where property owners request to change the
name of a road which has an existing city approved name, the property owners
may petition the City of Plummer to change such road name, subject to a fee as
set by the city council by resolution.
The petition must be presented no later than fifteen (15) days prior to the
regularly scheduled city council hearing, and contain the signatures of at
least fifty one percent (51%) of the property owners abutting the road under
consideration. Changing road names is deemed an administrative function, and
therefore, does not require a public hearing. Road names shall not be changed
more frequently than once every five (5) years. (Ord. 474, 12-19-2024)
5-8-4: SIGNING:
   A.   Physical Address Numbers: Physical address numbers shall be clearly
readable from the roadway, and shall contrast with background color pursuant to
the international fire code, as adopted by the City of Plummer. If a structure
is more than seventy-five feet (75') from the road, or is otherwise not clearly
visible from the road, its address shall be posted at the intersection of its
access road and public or private road. The address sign shall be no less than
four feet (4') nor more than six feet (6') above the ground on a substantial,
maintained support structure. The view of the address from the road must be
unobstructed and maintained.
   B.   Road Signs: Road signs shall be placed between six (6) and eight feet
(8') above the roadway, clearly visible at intersections. All primary letters,
numbers and symbols shall be a minimum of four inches (4") in height, with a
one-half inch (1/2") stroke, and shall be reflectorized and contrasting with
the background color of the sign in accordance with the manual of uniform
traffic control devices. Public road signs shall be green with white lettering.
Private road signs shall be blue, with white letters. All public and private
road signs shall be constructed and installed to the standards of the City of
Plummer and shall include the road name and address number derived from the
grid.
   C.   Road Sign Installation Standards: Standards for installation of road
signs is guided by the manual for uniform traffic control devices; however,
some additional criteria are needed to define specific circumstances:
      1.   Sign visibility requirements are set at a height of five feet (5')
minimum in rural areas and seven feet (7') in urban areas above the pavement.
      2.   Road signs placed for public roads shall be set by the City of
Plummer and shall meet the requirements of these standards.
      3.   Road signs may be mounted on the stop or yield sign posts with an
approved bracket and after receiving approval from the City of Plummer or Idaho
Transportation Department. (Ord. 474, 12-19-2024)
5-8-5: ENFORCEMENT:
