   A.   Violations: It shall be unlawful for any person to:
      1.   Erect or install a street name sign not in accordance with this
chapter;
      2.   Remove, alter, change, or deface a street name sign or address
identification erected or installed as provided herein;
      3.   Place or post addresses not approved by this chapter;
      4.   Fail to place an address visible from the street.
   B.   Penalties: Any person who violates or fails to comply with any of the
provisions of this chapter shall be guilty of an infraction punishable by a
fine of one hundred dollars ($100.00). In the event that violations of this
chapter are not corrected within fifteen (15) days of written notice, the City
of Plummer may perform the work and bill the property owners in accordance with
the laws of the State of Idaho. (Ord. 474, 12-19-2024)
TITLE 6
MUNICIPAL UTILITIES
CHAPTER 1
MUNICIPAL UTILITIES RATES
SECTION:
6-1-0: Municipal Utilities; Authority
6-1-1: Electrical Service Rates
6-1-2: Garbage Collection Rates
6-1-3: Water Service Rates
6-1-4: Sewer Use Rates
6-1-5: Hookup Fees
6-1-6: Electric Security Lights
6-1-0: MUNICIPAL UTILITIES; AUTHORITY:
The city of Plummer, county of Benewah, state of Idaho, hereby exercises its
lawful authority to establish and operate utility systems intended for the
delivery of water and electricity; for the collection and treatment of sewage
effluent; and for the collection and disposal of garbage and trash within the
city. No private individual, organization or agency may provide any such
services or utilities within the city limits of said city except by contract
with, or the prior written consent of, the Plummer city council, the city
retaining the authority to contract with individuals, agencies or organizations
to provide such services under the authority of the city. The use of such
services within the city limits of the city of Plummer is exclusive and
mandatory. (Ord. 368, 3-16-2005)
6-1-1: ELECTRICAL SERVICE RATES 1 :
   A.   The rates charged for electric energy hereafter supplied by the city to
its customers shall be reviewed annually by the city council and changed from
time to time by council resolution. The rate classifications shall be as
follows:
      1.   Residential rates.
      2.   Commercial and industrial rates.
      3.   Contract rates, which are negotiated and agreed upon by contract
between the two (2) parties.
      4.   Demand rate (not all commercial has a demand).
   B.   Service rates and rate classifications shall be included in a "rate
book" which shall be and remain on file in the office of the city clerk, which
book shall be available for public inspection. (1993 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See chapter 2 of this title for electrical service and additional fees.
6-1-2: GARBAGE COLLECTION RATES 1 :
The garbage collection rates shall be reviewed annually by the city council and
changed from time to time by council resolution. There are hereby established
the following types of collection rates:
   A.   Residential rates shall be based upon the number of automated
collection receptacles used for collection.
   B.   Commercial rates, with the following classifications:
      1.   Collection once or twice a week and number of automated collection
receptacles.
      2.   Collection once or twice a week and size of dumpster.
   C.   All bundled items and special hauls, as defined in section
3-5-6 of this code shall be assessed an overage charge. Any damage to or theft
of automated collection receptacles shall be assessed a repair or replacement
fee. (Ord. 427, 11-14-2013)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 3, chapter 5 of this code for garbage and refuse regulations.
6-1-3: WATER SERVICE RATES 1 :
The water service rates shall be reviewed annually by the city council and
changed from time to time by council resolution. The water service rate
classifications shall be residential, multi-unit residential, commercial and
industrial. (Ord. 383, 11-9-2006)
 
Notes
1 2. See chapter 4 of this title for billing procedures and chapter 5 of this
  title for water use regulations.
6-1-4: SEWER USE RATES 1 :
The sewer use rates shall be reviewed annually by the city council and changed
from time to time by council resolution.
The sewer use rate classifications shall be residential and commercial with the
commercial rates being based on average water usage. (Ord. 342, 5-10-2001)
 
Notes
1 3. See chapter 4 of this title for billing procedures and chapter 7 of this
  title for sewer use regulations.
6-1-5: HOOKUP FEES:
Hookup fees for residential electric, water and sewer services shall be as
determined annually by the city council. Commercial hookup fees shall be
determined based upon the need and availability of services. (1993 Code)
6-1-6: ELECTRIC SECURITY LIGHTS:
Electric security lights shall be available from the city, with the requirement
that the customer pay for the light upon installation and also pay a monthly
fee for the power and service expense. If repairs are needed, the customer
shall pay only for the parts needed and the city shall supply the labor without
a charge to the customer. (1993 Code)

6-2-2: AUTHORITY TO PROVIDE SERVICE:
   A.   The city may construct, reconstruct, enlarge, repair, alter and improve
its electric system or any part thereof and may supply the municipality and the
inhabitants thereof with light and/or power and charge therefor. Every lot or
building to which electric service is provided shall be subject to billing for
the service.
   B.   The city may supply electric power to persons (including municipal and
private corporations) outside the limits of the municipality and charge
therefor. Every lot or building to which electric service is provided shall be
subject to billing for the service.
   C.   The city shall use diligence to give continuance and uninterrupted
service, but in no case shall the city be liable to any customer, user or any
person or corporation because of any interruption in service.
   D.   Multiple Rental Units: Service charges for electrical service provided
to multiple rental units attached to a single meter shall be billed directly to
the landlord or property owner. (Ord. 443, 2-9-2017; amd. Ord. 463, 12-10-2020)
6-2-3: ELECTRICAL RATES:
Electrical rates within the city shall be as determined from time to time by
the city 1 . (Ord. 443, 2-9-2017; amd. Ord. 463, 12-10-2020)
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  6-1-1 of this title.
6-2-4: APPLICATION FOR CONNECTION AND CONTINUATION OF SERVICE:
   A.   Application for the use of electrical energy shall be made to the city
clerk, on approved forms. The applicant is responsible for the payment of all
charges, including the installation, connection, use and disconnect of any
electrical service.
   B.   All applications must also be signed by the owner of the real property
to be supplied with electrical service. By signing said application, the owner
of the real property agrees and consents to, and is responsible for, payment of
any and all charges for electrical service, including, but not limited to,
installation, connection, monthly use and disconnect charges.
   C.   Electrical power shall not be provided to any property except through a
watt hour meter installed by the city.
   D.   Electric services shall be connected and continued so long as there are
no arrearages owing for any utilities provided to the property, including
electric, water, sewer and garbage collection services. (Ord. 443, 2-9-2017;
amd. Ord. 463, 12-10-2020)
6-2-5: SERVICE CONNECTION REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Users must pay for all service connections, and additional lines shall
be built, and connections made only under such terms and conditions as the
mayor and city council may prescribe. All installations must be made under the
supervision of the city's electrical service provider., and all wiring must be
in accordance with the city's construction standards for electrical
connections, and national and state electrical codes and the national and state
electrical safety codes 1 .
   B.   If connection is requested by a property owner in good standing, a
meter installation charge of twenty five dollars ($25.00) will be collected to
connect a meter during normal business hours; and a reconnection charge of
fifty dollars ($50.00) will be collected for any meter installed outside of
normal business hours shall be charged and will be due and owing Immediately.
   C.   When a meter is disconnected, whether by customer request or for reason
of nonpayment, there shall be a disconnection charge of thirty-five dollars
($35.00) collected to cover the cost of disconnecting the meter. Meters will be
disconnected only during normal business hours.
   D.   No connection, reconnection or reinstatement of electric services shall
be made unless and until all prior unpaid utility service charges (including
electrical, water, sewer and garbage collection charges and fees) have been
paid in full. (Ord. 443, 2-9-2017; amd. Ord. 463, 12-10-2020)
 
Notes
1 1. IC §39-4109.
6-2-6: BILLING DEPOSIT:
(Rep. by Ord. 471, 10-12-2023)
6-2-7: MAINTENANCE OF DEPOSITS:
(Rep. by Ord. 471, 10-12-2023)
6-2-8: BILLING PROCEDURES:
   A.   Due Date; Past Due Account: All billing for electrical service shall be
due on the tenth (10) day of the month and shall be considered past due after
that date.
   B.   Notification to Property Owners: In the event a past due account is in
the name of another who is not the owner of the real property being serviced,
the city may notify the owner of the real property of the delinquency.
   C.   Separate Billings: Charges for each month of electrical service shall
constitute a separate sale of a commodity (electrical power), shall constitute
a separate billable item, and two (2) or more unpaid charges, if allowed to
accumulate, shall not be deemed an "open account." (Ord. 443, 2-9-2017; amd.
Ord. 463, 12-10-2020)
6-2-9: DELINQUENT ACCOUNTS:
   A.   Past Due Accounts: Electrical service shall be terminated at twelve
o'clock (12:00) noon on the twenty-third day of any month for any property for
which the billing for electrical service is past due on such date. At the time
that the service is terminated, the meter at the service site shall be removed
by the city.
   B.   Late Fees: All accounts that have a balance of ten dollars ($10.00) and
are thirty (30) days past due shall be charged a late fee of one percent (1%)
per month with a minimum of ten dollars ($10.00) per month.
   C.   Returned Check Fee: A returned check fee shall be added to all accounts
for which a check is returned from the bank for any reason not the fault of the
city. The fee shall be set by resolution of the Plummer City Council, and such
fee shall apply separately to each check which is returned from the bank. The
city can refuse to accept future personal checks from customers whose check has
been returned by the bank for any reason not the fault of the city. (Ord. 443,
2-9-2017; amd. Ord. 463, 12-10-2020)
6-2-10: CONNECTION OF RENTAL UNITS:
   A.   Except for multiple rentals units connected to a single meter, which
shall only be connected or disconnected at the property owner's request,
electrical service shall not be connected to a rental unit until both the
tenant and the property owner have signed the application form as provided for
in section
6-2-3 of this chapter.
   B.   When a tenant requests a final power reading, the meter will be
disconnected, except as provided for in subsection C of this section. Anyone
wishing to have service reconnected, including the landlord or the property
owner, will have to apply as provided in this chapter.
   C.   A landlord or property owner may, in writing, request that the city
allow electrical services to continue unabated even when his rental units are
unoccupied. In such case, it will be the responsibility of the property owner
to notify the city clerk, in writing when a new tenant moves in so that a
proper application for service can be required of the new tenant. The landlord
or property owner shall be responsible for all service between the time of the
final reading for the departing tenant and completion of proper application by,
acceptance of, the new tenant by the city, including the payment by the new
tenant of all necessary deposits, fees and charges.
   D.   The landlord and/or property owner shall be liable for any unpaid
charges or fees on any rental unit owned by the property owner. (Ord. 443, 2-9-
2017; amd. Ord. 463, 12-10-2020)
6-2-11: TEMPORARY DISCONTINUANCE OF SERVICE, CHARGES 1 :
   A.   In the event that any customer or user of electrical power provided by
the city shall desire a temporary discontinuation of said service, and shall
desire that the city discontinue the same, he shall pay a fee of thirty five
dollars ($35.00) for disconnection of service and twenty five dollars ($25.00)
when the service is reestablished. During the period of disconnection, the
customer shall be responsible for paying the base rate for the service provided
or available for use.
   B.   A service charge of twenty-five ($25.00) shall be made for restoring
electrical service when said service has been disconnected for any reason.
(Ord. 443, 2-9-2017; amd. Ord. 463, 12-10-2020)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section 6-3-8 of this title.
6-2-12: PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   Tampering With Meters 1 : If any user of electrical energy or any other
person, in any manner, tampers with any meter in such manner that such meter
does not measure or report the full amount of electric energy supplied to a
customer, he shall guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction thereof, shall
be subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code.
   B.   Resale of Electric Energy: No electric energy sold to any user may be
resold.
   C.   Interference with Service: If any user uses electric energy in any
manner that causes fluctuations that interfere with the normal use of
electricity by other users, such user shall be required to install equipment to
remedy such fluctuations at his own expense, and upon his failure to do so, the
service may be discontinued to such user.
   D.   Damage to Property: Anyone who shall, in any manner, injure any poles,
wires, insulators or transformers or, in any manner, tamper with or injure any
of the equipment or apparatus of the electric light system of the city shall be
guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to
penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 443, 2-9-2017; amd. Ord. 463, 12-10-2020)
 
Notes
1 1. See also subsection 6-3-5D of this title.
CHAPTER 3
ELECTRIC USE REGULATIONS 1
SECTION:
6-3-1: Compliance Required
6-3-2: Application For Electric Use
6-3-3: Use Of Electricity Restricted
6-3-4: Connections To System; General Metering Requirements
6-3-5: Electric Meters Supplied By City
6-3-6: Electric Rates
6-3-7: Right Of Entry For Inspection Purposes
6-3-8: Disconnection Of Service
6-3-9: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. See also chapter 2 of this title.
6-3-1: COMPLIANCE REQUIRED:
The provisions of this chapter must be strictly complied with in every
instance, and electric service must be paid for by all owners of premises
supplied according to the schedule of electric rates 1 . Employees of the city
are not permitted to make any exceptions whatever. (1993 Code)
 
Notes
1 2. See section
  6-2-3 of this title.
6-3-2: APPLICATION FOR ELECTRIC USE:
Applications for the use of and connection for new electrical service must be
made on printed forms to be furnished by the city at city hall. The applicant
must state fully and truly for what purpose the electricity is required, the
amp service that is being serviced and whether service will be overhead or
underground. In all cases, the owner of the property to which the power is
supplied will be held responsible for payment of all charges and rentals for
the use of same. (1993 Code)
6-3-3: USE OF ELECTRICITY RESTRICTED:
No person supplied with electricity from the city will be entitled to the use
of electricity for any other purpose than those stated in his application or to
apply in any way to other persons, families or places. (1993 Code)
6-3-4: CONNECTIONS TO SYSTEM; GENERAL METERING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Breaking Of Meter Seals:
      1.   The purpose of seals placed on meters by the city is for the safety
and/or prevention of tampering.
      2.   Under normal circumstances, only Plummer personnel shall remove the
seals. It is the customer's responsibility to notify the city prior to the
removal of meter seals for any reason. Seals may be removed only in an
emergency. The city must be notified as soon as possible thereafter. Seals must
not be cut.
      3.   Caution: With some types of meter bases, removal of the meter does
not deenergize the service. On instrument transformer metering, secondary
current leads may develop high potential with meter removed and transformer not
shorted.
      4.   Any person who cuts utility seals and/or wrongfully obtains electric
service by bypassing, tampering with or modifying a meter may be convicted of a
crime.
      5.   No jumpering of meter sockets by electricians or customers is
allowed for any reason.
   B.   Meeting The Requirements:
      1.   Whenever any changes, alterations or additions are made to any
electrical service, all the metering must meet current city standards. This
will include location and equipment.
      2.   All commercial and industrial accounts must have manual circuit
closing sockets.
      3.   All temporary power used by contractors must be metered.
Single meters shall be installed between five feet (5') and six feet (6') to
the top of the meter above the floor or finished grade. Exceptions will be
meter modules and pedestal meters which shall be positioned for ease of
reading.
      4.   Meters and transformer enclosures shall be installed outdoors except
by special permission from the utility. If permission is granted for inside
metering, the requirements are:
         a.   Exterior door with direct access to meters.
         b.   If locked, a key and lock box mounting space must be provided.
         c.   Area must be well lit and not used for storage.
         d.   Meters must be installed.
         e.   Meters must be installed at the service equipment and not
separated by walls or partitions.
         f.   Access during business hours.
         g.   Access during all hours depending on utility.
      5.   No metering equipment shall be installed at a serviced switch
located in an inaccessible place such as a manhole or in a vault.
      6.   When meter modules are installed, the maximum height will be six
feet (6') and the minimum height will be two feet (2').
      7.   Multiple meters in one building, with several tenants, shall be
grouped in only one accessible location; one meter space, each with its own
disconnect.
      8.   Metered and nonmetered circuits shall not be run in the same raceway
or conduit. (The city may permit the aforesaid with prior approval.)
      9.   Meters must be protected from ice or snow sliding off metal roofs by
extending eaves, gutter or other means. Meters must also be protected from
physical damage.
      10.   All enclosures provided by the customer shall be approved by the
city.
      11.   Meter equipment shall be located on the lineside of the main
disconnect.
      12.   Exception: When there are more than six (6) meters, they shall be
located on the loadside of the main disconnect, if a main disconnect is
required, (which shall be sealable) and on the lineside of the individual
service switches.
      13.   Customers or contractors are not authorized to relocate any meter
belonging to the city or interfere with the meter or its connections without
prior city approval.
   C.   Identification:
      1.   When more than one meter is installed at one location, the installer
shall clearly mark each socket and unit in suitable, acceptable, permanent
lettering with the correct address or number of the building area served by
that meter.
      2.   The building owner shall be responsible for proper identification.
      3.   Service will not be established until marking is complete.
      4.   All cabinets, gutters, sockets and associated devices on the
lineside of the meter must have provision for sealing or locking by the city
and shall remain sealed at all times.
      5.   Whenever additions, alterations or changes are made on systems
having meter installations not in accordance with this section, the customer
shall properly relocate the metering equipment.
      6.   Ample workspace shall be provided for the metering and kept clear at
all times. Minimum space shall be thirty inches (30") wide with the meter
centered. Minimal frontal and overhead clearances shall be per national
electrical code.
   D.   Meter Mounting:
      1.   Meter sockets and/or enclosures must be plumb and level and securely
mounted to a rigid surface. All conductors must be securely fastened and shall
not interfere with the operation of the meter or circuit closing device.
      2.   The customer shall provide space for metering, convenient to the
city, readily accessible, free from vibration, corrosive atmosphere, abnormal
temperatures and well lit. If, in the opinion of the City, a meter is made
inaccessible, such as by the installation of a fence or enclosure, the customer
shall, at his expense, move the meter socket to an accessible location. The
City, at its option, may install a remote reading register or a pole meter to
alleviate an accessibility problem, at the customer's expense, in accordance
with the City's schedule of charges.
   E.   Disconnects: Outside disconnects will be required on the loadside of
the meter, unless given prior approval from the utility.
   F.   Services: All services will be installed per the National Electrical
Code and will be inspected by the Idaho State Electrical Inspector.
   G.   Residential, Single-Family Dwellings:
      1.   The City will accept most UL listed meter bases up to 200 amp
capacity.
      2.   320/400 amp meter sockets will be accepted on most 400 amp
residential services.
      3.   The City should be contacted for specific requirements.
      4.   Refer to subsections A through F of this Section for requirements
such as location, heights, etc.
   H.   Residential, Multi-Family Dwellings:
      1.   The City may require a house meter for common use facilities such as
hall lights, laundry rooms, etc.
      2.   The City may require manual circuit-closing meter bases on the house
meter.
      3.   Refer to subsections A through F of this Section for requirements on
locations, identification, etc.
   I.   Commercial (Up to 200 Amp), Single-Phase or Three-Phase:
      1.   Manual circuit-closing meter bases are required on all commercial
accounts.
      2.   Manual circuit-closing sockets are not required on 200 amp single-
phase temporary service.
      3.   Gang type or module type meter banks must have manual circuit
closing by-pass.
      4.   Refer to subsections A through F of this Section for requirements on
locations.
   J.   Temporary Services:
      1.   Single-phase manual circuit closing (MCC) is not required.
      2.   All temporary services must be metered.
      3.   Three-phase services require manual circuit closing.
      4.   Single-phase 12/208 wye temporary socket must have five (5)
terminals.
   K.   Commercial Over 200 Amps, Single-Phase and Three-Phase:
      1.   CT metering required if greater than 200 amp commercial.
      2.   Above 20 amp, three-phase, CT meter will be required.
      3.   All metering equipment will be mounted by the customer. This
includes sockets, CT enclosures and metering conduit, unless otherwise
specified.
      4.   The City may allow CTs to be mounted inside underground (URD)
distribution transformers.
      5.   Meters must be located within thirty feet (30') of the CTs as
measured by wire length, or by special permission of the City.
      6.   Meter conduit must be one inch (1") and run directly from
transformers to the meter socket or enclosure.
      7.   On underground (URD) services a CT enclosure may also become the
point of connection by the City.
      8.   Metering must be located as close to the City's distribution as
possible.
      9.   All instrument metering wire shall be copper, preferably solid,
color coded the entire length and shall run without splice or fuse. Colored
phase tape will not be accepted.
      10.   If meter wire is to be provided, it shall extend at least five feet
(5') from the weather head and at least four feet (4') into the meter socket or
enclosure.
      11.   On overhead (OH) services, CTs may be mounted on or adjacent to the
mast head or in a CT enclosure and usually are mounted by the city.
      12.   The meter instrument transformers are provided by the city.
      13.   The customer must provide space for metering that is convenient to
the city. Consideration must be given to the meter readers, service
technicians, etc.
      14.   On large inductive loads KVAR metering may be required. Check with
the city. (1993 Code)
6-3-5: ELECTRIC METERS SUPPLIED BY CITY:
   A.   Electric meters will be installed by the city upon application therefor
as hereinafter provided.
   B.   Meters will be supplied by the city and remain the property of the
city.
   C.   When a meter is installed on any property, meters shall only be removed
by the city.
   D.   Any person found guilty of tampering with meters 1  shall be subject to
penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1993 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also subsection 6-2-12A of this title.
6-3-6: ELECTRIC RATES:
See section
6-2-3 of this title for electrical rates. (1993 Code)
6-3-7: RIGHT OF ENTRY FOR INSPECTION PURPOSES:
   A.   Inspection Of Lines And Meters: The city shall have access, at all
reasonable times and hours, to all parts of any building or premises in which
electric service is supplied, for the purpose of inspecting the city lines to
the meter and the meter itself.
   B.   Reading Meters: The city shall have access to the meter for the purpose
of reading said meter for billing purposes each month, and the owner or
occupant is responsible for keeping said access open at all times for the meter
reader. Meters shall be so placed for easy access and readability, with no
obstructions or deterrents such as locked gates. The owner of the premises
shall also be responsible for keeping dogs confined a safe distance from the
meter, for protection of the meter reader. (1993 Code)
6-3-8: DISCONNECTION OF SERVICE 1 :
Any customer or user of electrical power provided by the city who wishes to
permanently disconnect service may do so upon two (2) days' written notice in
writing to city hall and payment of a fee for removal of the drop lines to the
meter base. (1993 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section 6-2-11 of this title for temporary disconnection.
6-3-9: PENALTY:
Any person who shall violate any provision of this chapter shall be subject to
penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1993 Code)
CHAPTER 4
WATER, SEWER AND GARBAGE UTILITIES 1
SECTION:
6-4-1: Definitions
6-4-2: Authority To Provide Service
6-4-3: Water, Sewer And Garbage Collection Rates
6-4-4: Application For, Connection And Continuation Of Water, Sewer And Garbage
Collection Services
6-4-5: Billing Deposit (Rep. by Ord. 471, 10-12-2023)
6-4-6: Maintenance Of Deposits (Rep. by Ord. 471, 10-12-2023)
6-4-7: Billing Procedures
6-4-8: Delinquent Accounts
6-4-9: Connection Of Rental Units
 
Notes
1 1. See chapters 5 and 7 of this title.
6-4-1: DEFINITIONS:
CITY: The city of Plummer, in the county of Benewah, state of Idaho.
GENDER: Where the masculine gender is used in this chapter, it shall include
the feminine.
METER: A gallon per day meter or similar meter installed for the purpose of
measuring water usage.
PROPERTY OWNER IN GOOD STANDING: The owner of the real property to which water,
sewer and garbage collection services are provided or requested to be provided,
who has paid all of his personal city utility billings (including electrical,
water, sewer and garbage collection charges and fees) in a timely manner for
the preceding twelve (12) months and who has not, within the past five (5)
years, caused the city to suffer a loss as a result of the discharge of any
city bill in bankruptcy proceedings.
RENTAL UNIT: A house or land which is occupied by one who does not own both the
house and the land and shall include, within its definition, all mobile homes
which are not affixed to a permanent foundation, without regard to ownership or
title to the land or mobile home. (Ord. 442, 2-9-2017)
6-4-2: AUTHORITY TO PROVIDE SERVICE:
   A.   Coverage: Every lot or building to which water, sewer and garbage
collection services are available shall be subject to billing for the service
and for the availability of the service.
   B.   Multiple Rental Units: Service charges for water, sewer and garbage
collection services provided to multiple rental units attached to a single
meter shall be billed directly to the landlord or property owner. (Ord. 442, 2-
9-2017)
6-4-3: WATER, SEWER AND GARBAGE COLLECTION RATES:
Water, sewer and garbage collection rates within the city shall be as
determined, from time to time, by the city council 1 . (Ord. 442, 2-9-2017)
 
Notes
  1. See sections
1 6-1-2,
  6-1-3 and
  6-1-4 of this title.
6-4-4: APPLICATION FOR, CONNECTION AND CONTINUATION OF WATER, SEWER AND GARBAGE
COLLECTION SERVICES:
   A.   Applications for the use of water, sewer and garbage collection
services shall be made to the city clerk on approved forms. The applicant is
responsible for all charges.
   B.   All applications must be signed by the owner of the real property to be
supplied with water, sewer and garbage collection services. By signing said
application, the owner of the real property agrees and consents to, and is
responsible for, payment of any and all charges for water, sewer and garbage
collection services, including, but not limited to, meter installation and
monthly charges.
   C.   Water shall not be provided to any property except through a gallons
per day meter installed by the city.
   D.   If connection is requested by a property owner in good standing, a
meter installation charge shall be charged. Applications shall be subject to a
billing deposit, as described in this chapter.
   E.   No connection, reconnection or reinstatement of water or sewer
services, or provision of garbage services, shall be made unless and until all
prior unpaid utility service charges (including electrical, water, sewer and
garbage charges and fees) have been paid in full.
   F.   Water, sewer and garbage services shall be continued so long as there
are no arrearages owing for any utilities provided to the property, including
electrical, water, sewer and garbage collection services. (Ord. 442, 2-9-2017)
6-4-5: BILLING DEPOSIT:
(Rep. by Ord. 471, 10-12-2023)
6-4-6: MAINTENANCE OF DEPOSITS:
(Rep. by Ord. 471, 10-12-2023)
6-4-7: BILLING PROCEDURES:
   A.   Due Date; Past Due Account: All billings for water, sewer and garbage
collection service shall be due on the tenth day of the month and shall be
considered past due after that date.
   B.   Separate Billings: Charges for each month of water service, sewer
service or garbage collection service or availability of such services shall
constitute separate sales of services and shall constitute separate billable
items, and two (2) or more unpaid charges, if allowed to accumulate, shall not
be deemed an "open account".
   C.   Notification To Property Owners: In the event a past due account is in
the name of another who is not the owner of the real property being serviced,
the city may notify the owner of the real property of the delinquency. (Ord.
442, 2-9-2017)
6-4-8: DELINQUENT ACCOUNTS:
   A.   Past Due Accounts: Water, sewer and garbage services shall be
terminated at twelve o'clock (12:00) noon three (3) days after the electric
services is disconnected for any property for which the billing for such
services is past due. Water may be disconnected if a sewer leak is detected on
the property owner's sewer system.
   B.   Late Fee: All accounts thirty (30) days past due shall be charged a
late fee of one percent (1%) per month with a minimum of ten dollars ($10.00)
per month.
   C.   Returned Check Fee: A returned check fee shall be added to all accounts
for which a check is returned from the bank for any reason not the fault of the
city. The fee shall be set by resolution of the Plummer city council, and such
fee shall apply separately to each check which is returned from the bank. The
city can refuse to accept future personal checks from customers whose check has
been returned by the bank for any reason not the fault of the city. (Ord. 442,
2-9-2017)
6-4-9: CONNECTION OF RENTAL UNITS:
   A.   Excepting multiple rental units connected to a single meter, which
shall only be commenced or terminated at the property owner's request, water,
sewer and garbage collection services shall not be commenced to a rental unit
until both the tenant and property owner have signed an application form and
submitted said application form to the city clerk.
   B.   No water service or garbage collection service will be connected,
reconnected or reinstated, unless and until all prior unpaid utility service
charges for the property owner and the tenant (including electrical, water,
sewer and garbage collection charges and fees) have been paid in full. (Ord.
442, 2-9-2017)
CHAPTER 5
WATER USE REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-5-1: Compliance Required
6-5-2: Application for Water Use
6-5-3: Use of Water Restricted
6-5-4: Connections to System
6-5-5: Water Meters
6-5-6: Water Rates
6-5-7: Right of Entry for Inspection Purposes
6-5-8: Disconnection of Service
6-5-9: Use of Water for Sprinkling Purposes
6-5-10: Prohibited Acts and Conditions
6-5-11: Penalty
6-5-1: COMPLIANCE REQUIRED:
The provisions of this Chapter must be strictly complied with in every
instance, and water must be paid for by all owners of premises supplied
according to the schedule of water rates 1 . Employees of the City are not
permitted to make any exceptions whatever. (Ord. 21, 1-20-13)
 
Notes
1 1. See Section 6–1–3 of this Title.
6-5-2: APPLICATION FOR WATER USE:
Applications for the use of water must be made on printed forms to be furnished
by the City at the office of the City Hall. The applicant must state fully and
truly for what purpose the water is required. In all cases, the owner of the
property to which water is supplied will be held responsible for payment of all
charges and rentals for the use of same. (Ord. 21, 1-20-13; 1993 Code)
6-5-3: USE OF WATER RESTRICTED:
No person supplied with water from the City main will be entitled to the use of
water for any other purposes than those stated in his application or to apply
in any way to other persons, families or places. (Ord. 21, 1-20-13)
6-5-4: CONNECTIONS TO SYSTEM:
   A.   All service pipes must be so arranged that the supply to each separate
house or premises may be controlled by a separate stopcock placed within and
near the line of the street curb, and one person must pay for all water used
through said service pipe for his own use only. (Ord. 21, 1-20-13)
   B.   Water will not be furnished where there are defective pipes or
appurtenant equipment or where there are valves or tanks without self-acting
float valves and stop waste valves at each hydrant and house connection. When
such may be discovered, the water shall be shut off from such premises after
seventy two (72) hours' notice except under emergency situations when no notice
shall be necessary, and not turned on again until the owner or occupant has
made the necessary repairs.
   C.   When a permit has been granted for the installation of water, a
corporation cock or trap will be inserted in the main. The tap shall be of such
size as the City may consider proper for the supply of water needed. (Ord. 21,
1-20-13; 1993 Code)
   D.   The tap shall be inserted by the City and the hookup fee which had been
paid in advance shall cover the installation of the tap, the service line to
the property line up to but not exceeding forty feet (40'), a meter, meter
housing, meter corp and backflow prevention device. This fee also covers the
labor to install the aforementioned items. Any additional footage or
extenuating circumstances will be additional charges and the City will not be
responsible to extend the line onto the property.
   E.   If a main line does not exist on an already annexed and developed
street, the City will extend the water main at its expense. However, if the
property is part of a new development, the expense of the main line extension
will be of the developer or property owner.
   F.   No plumber or any other person will be allowed to make connections with
the City mains or to make alterations in conduit, pipe or other fixtures
connected therewith, to connect pipes when they have been disconnected or to
turn water on or off on any premises without permission from the City. (1993
Code)
6-5-5: WATER METERS:
   A.   Remote water meters will be installed by the City with location of the
remote to be accessible to the meter reader upon application therefor as
hereinafter provided.
   B.   Meters will be supplied by the City, the cost of which is part of the
hookup fee.
   C.   When installed on any property, meters shall only be removed by the
City. For the violation of this provision, the water shall be turned off and a
fine imposed as provided in Section
1-4-1 of this Code. Said fine must be paid before the water is again turned on.
   D.   When a meter or indicator gets out of order or fails to register
correctly, the charge shall be according to the average quantity of water used
daily as shown by the meter when in order. (Ord. 21, 1-20-13; 1993 Code)
6-5-6: WATER RATES:
   A.   Water rates shall be as established in Section 6–1–3 of this Title.
   B.   The rates prescribed shall apply to all structures, homes and buildings
or other units wherein an independent water connection is in use. If multiple
users are on one meter, the account shall be the responsibility of the property
owner or landlord.
   C.   The water rates established shall be paid as billed and required by the
City, as provided in Chapter 4 of this Title, and the City retains authority to
make any amendments to or additions or corrections to the rates by Council
action or by resolution and specifically retains the right to enter into
contract or agreement with respect to revised water rates with any water users,
water district, individuals or corporations outside the City. (Ord. 290, 9-14-
89; 1993 Code)
6-5-7: RIGHT OF ENTRY FOR INSPECTION PURPOSES:
The City shall have access, at all reasonable times and hours, to all parts of
any building or premises in which water is being delivered from the water
mains, for the purpose of inspecting the condition of the pipes and fixtures
and the manner in which the water is used. (Ord. 21, 1-20-13)
6-5-8: DISCONNECTION OF SERVICE:
   A.   Should it be desired to discontinue the use of water supplied to the
premises, not less than two (2) days' notice, in writing, must be given to the
City, unless shutoff is for an emergency.
   B.   The water may, at any time, be shut off from the mains, without notice,
for repairs or for any other necessary purpose, and the City will not be
responsible or liable for any subsequent damage. In all cases where
practicable, the City shall give the consumers notice before the water is shut
off from the mains; provided, however, that when a fire alarm is sounded or
turned on, all persons using water for sprinkling shall at once turn the water
off.
   C.   After the water has been shut off at the stopcock, it shall not be
turned on again by any person, except by direction of the City and until the
charge is paid for the expense of shutting off the water and turning it on
again. (Ord. 21, 1-20-13; 1993 Code)
6-5-9: USE OF WATER FOR SPRINKLING PURPOSES:
Any and all persons using a meter has a right, at any and all times, to use
water for sprinkling purposes. However, the Mayor and City Council reserve the
right to stop all sprinkling in case of shortage of water. Sprinkling streets,
under any circumstances, is forbidden, except by the City. (Ord. 21, 1-20-13;
1993 Code)
6-5-10: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   No person shall place upon or cover any hydrants, water gate, stopcock
or meter connected with the water pipes of the City with any building material
or other substance so as to prevent the free access to the same at all times.
   B.   No person shall meddle with or use or disturb any of the property,
tools, machinery or other appliances belonging or appertaining to the Water
Department or to use or remove any fire plug or meter or turn water through the
same.
   C.   No person shall have a meter to use water from the City mains or from
any probate service pipe without applying to and getting assistance from the
City. (Ord. 21, 1-20-13; 1993 Code)
6-5-11: PENALTY:
Any person violating this Chapter in any particular or causing damage to the
water system shall be debarred from making connections with the City mains and
shall, upon conviction thereof, be punished as provided in Section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 21, 1-20-13; 1993 Code)
CHAPTER 6
CROSS CONNECTIONS
SECTION:
6-6-1: Purpose and Scope
6-6-2: Definitions
6-6-3: Protection of Water Supply
6-6-4: Use of Backflow Prevention Devices
6-6-5: Cross Connection Inspections
6-6-6: Installation Permits
6-6-7: Additional Remedies
6-6-8: Violations and Penalties
6-6-1: PURPOSE AND SCOPE:
The purpose of this Chapter is to protect the public health of water consumers
by the control of actual and/or potential cross connections. (1993 Code)
6-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this Chapter, unless the context otherwise requires, the following
words and terms shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this Section:
BACKFLOW: The flow, other than the intended direction of flow, of any foreign
liquids, gases or substances into the distribution system of a public water
supply.
BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICE: A device to counteract back pressure or prevent
back siphonage.
CONTAMINATION: The entry into or presence in a public water supply of any
substances which may be deleterious to health and/or quality of the water.
CROSS CONNECTION: Any physical arrangement whereby a public water supply is
connected, directly or indirectly, with any other water supply system, sewer,
drain, conduit, pool, storage reservoir, plumbing fixture or other device which
contains or may contain contaminated water, sewage or other waste or liquids of
unknown or unsafe quality which may be capable of imparting contamination to
the public water supply as a result of backflow.
DIRECTOR: The Director of the Department of Health and Welfare of the State of
Idaho or his authorized agent.
ENGINEER: The engineer under contract with the City who shall be a registered
professional engineer in the State of Idaho.
HEALTH OFFICER: The State of Idaho Department of Health and Welfare Health
Officer or other authorized agent.
PUBLIC WATER SUPPLY: Any system of water supply intended or used for human
consumption or other domestic uses, including source, treatment, storage,
transmission and distribution facilities, where water is furnished to any
collection or number of individuals or is made available to the public for
human consumption or domestic use.
PURVEYOR: The City of Plummer or its authorized agent.
REGULATIONS: The Idaho Regulations for Public Drinking Water Systems, November
1977, Division of Environment, Department of Health and Welfare, State of
Idaho, and as may be subsequently amended or modified.
SUPERINTENDENT: The Superintendent of Public Works of the City of Plummer or
his authorized agent. (1993 Code)
6-6-3: PROTECTION OF WATER SUPPLY:
No water service connection to any premises shall be installed or continued in
use by the purveyor unless the water supply is protected by backflow prevention
devices whenever required by this Chapter. The installation or maintenance of a
cross connection which will endanger the water quality of the potable water
supply of the City shall be unlawful and is prohibited and shall be penalized
as hereinafter provided. Any such cross connection now existing or hereafter
installed is hereby declared to be a public nuisance, and the same shall be
abated as provided by law for any public nuisance 1 . The control or
elimination of the cross connections shall be in accordance with this Chapter
and the Regulations, together with the latest edition of appropriate manuals of
standard practice pertaining to cross connection control, approved by the
Superintendent. The engineer shall have the authority to establish requirements
more stringent than State regulations if he deems that the conditions so
dictate. Such requirements shall be published and available to the public at
the City Hall. The purveyor shall adopt and publish rules and regulations as
necessary to carry out the provisions of this Chapter and shall have such rules
and regulations available in published form to the public. (1993 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. I.C. §§52-205 and 52-206; see also Section 3–4–4 of this Code.
6-6-4: USE OF BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICES:
   A.   Backflow prevention devices shall be installed at the ties on the
premises or the material used in connection with service connections or within
any premises where, in the judgment of the purveyor or the Health Officer, the
nature and extent of the activities or the materials stored on the premises
would present an immediate and dangerous hazard to health and/or be deleterious
to the quality of the water should a cross connection occur, even though such
cross connection does not exist at the time the backflow prevention device
shall be installed under circumstances including, but not limited to, the
following:
      1.   Premises having an auxiliary water supply, unless the quality of the
auxiliary supply is in compliance with the Regulations and is acceptable to the
purveyor.
      2.   Premises having internal cross connections that are not correctable,
or intricate plumbing arrangements which make it impracticable to ascertain
whether or not cross connections exist.
      3.   Premises where entry is restricted so that inspections for cross
connections cannot be made with sufficient frequency or at sufficiently short
notice to assure that cross connections do not exist.
      4.   Premises having a repeated history of cross connections being
established or re-established.
      5.   Premises on which any substance is handled under pressure so as to
permit entry into the public water supply or where a cross connection could
reasonably be expected to occur. This shall include the handling of process
waters and cooling waters.
      6.   Premises where materials of a toxic or hazardous nature are handled
in such a manner that if back siphonage should occur, a serious health hazard
might result.
      7.   The following types of facilities will fall into one of the above
categories where a backflow prevention device is required to protect the public
water supply. A backflow prevention device shall be installed at these
facilities unless the purveyor and the Superintendent determine that no hazard
exists:
         Hospitals, mortuaries, clinics
         Laboratories
         Metal plating industries
         Sewage treatment plants
         Food or beverage processing plants
         Chemical plants using a water process
         Petroleum processing or storage plants
         Radioactive material processing plants
         Others specified by the Superintendent
      8.   Other premises, as specified by the engineer, Superintendent or
Health Officer, where backflow prevention devices are required to protect the
public water supply.
   B.   The type of protective device required shall depend on the degree of
hazard which exists:
      1.   An air-gap separation or a reduced pressure principle backflow
prevention device shall be installed where the public water supply may be
contaminated with sewage, industrial waste of a toxic nature or other
contaminant which could cause a health or system hazard.
      2.   In the case of a substance which may be objectionable but not
hazardous to health, a double check valve assembly, air-gap separation or a
reduced pressure principle backflow prevention device shall be installed.
   C.   Backflow prevention devices required by this Chapter shall be installed
at the meter, at the property line of the premises when meters are not used or
at a location designated by the purveyor. The device shall be located so as to
be readily accessible for maintenance and testing and, furthermore, where no
part of the device will be submerged.
   D.   Backflow prevention devices required by this Chapter shall be installed
under the supervision of and with the approval of the purveyor.
   E.   Any protective device required by this Chapter shall be a model
approved by the engineer. A double check valve assembly or a reduced pressure
principle backflow prevention device will be approved if it has successfully
passed performance tests of the University of Southern California Engineering
Center or other testing laboratories satisfactory to the Superintendent and the
engineer. These devices shall be furnished and installed by and at the expense
of the customer.
   F.   Backflow prevention devices installed pursuant to this Chapter, except
atmospheric vacuum breakers, shall be inspected and tested annually or more
often if necessary. Inspections, tests and maintenance shall be at the
customer's expense. Whenever the devices are found to be defective, they shall
be repaired, overhauled or replaced at the customer's expense. Inspections,
tests, repairs and records thereof shall be accomplished under the purveyor's
supervision by certified testers.
   G.   No underground sprinkling device will be installed without adequate
backflow prevention devices at the point from which the water for irrigation is
taken from the public water supply.
   H.   Failure of the customer to cooperate in the installation, maintenance,
testing or inspection of backflow prevention devices required by this Chapter
and the Regulations shall be grounds for termination of water service to the
premises or, in the alternative, the installation of an air-gap separation at
the customer's expense. (1993 Code)
6-6-5: CROSS CONNECTION INSPECTIONS:
   A.   No water shall be delivered to any structure hereafter built within the
City or within areas served by the City water until the same shall have been
inspected by the purveyor for possible cross connections and have been approved
as being free of the same.
   B.   Any construction for industrial or other purposes which is classified
as hazardous facilities pursuant to subsection
6–6–4A7 hereof, where it is reasonable to anticipate intermittent cross
connections, or as determined by the Superintendent, shall be protected by the
installation of one or more backflow prevention devices at the point of service
from the public water supply or any other location designated by the purveyor.
   C.   Inspections shall be made periodically of all buildings, structures or
improvements of any nature now receiving water through the City's system for
the purpose of ascertaining whether cross connections exist. Such inspections
shall be made by the purveyor. (1993 Code)
6-6-6: INSTALLATION PERMITS:
If cross connection control devices are found to be necessary, the owner of the
property served must apply to the purveyor for a specific installation permit.
(1993 Code)
6-6-7: ADDITIONAL REMEDIES:
In the event an improper cross connection is not corrected within the time
limit set by the Superintendent, or in the event the purveyor is refused access
to any property for the purpose of determining whether or not cross connections
exist, delivery of water to the property shall cease until the deficiency is
corrected to the purveyor's satisfaction. In addition, the purveyor may effect
the necessary repairs or modifications at the expense of the property owner and
refuse delivery of water to the property until the cost thereof shall have been
paid. (1993 Code)
6-6-8: VIOLATIONS AND PENALTIES:
Any person who violates, disobeys, omits, neglects or refuses to comply with or
resists the enforcement of any of the provisions of this Chapter or the Rules
and Regulations as adopted by this Chapter shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall, for each offense, be punished
by a fine as provided in Section
1–4–1 of this Code. (1993 Code)
CHAPTER 7
SEWER USE REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-7-1: Definitions
6-7-2: Use Of Public Sewers Required
6-7-3: Private Sewage Disposal
6-7-4: Sewer Use Rates
6-7-5: Building Sewers And Connections
6-7-6: Use Of The Public Sewers
6-7-7: Grease, Oil Or Sediment Separators
6-7-8: Powers And Authority Of Inspectors
6-7-9: Penalties
6-7-10: Protection From Damage
6-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the meanings of terms used
in this chapter shall be as follows:
BOD (Denoting Biochemical Oxygen Demand): The quantity of oxygen utilized in
the biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory
procedures in five (5) days at twenty degrees centigrade (20°C), expressed in
milligrams per liter.
BUILDING DRAIN: That part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system
which receives the discharge from soil, waste and other drainage pipes inside
the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer, beginning five
feet (5') outside the inner face of the building wall.
BUILDING SEWER: The extension from the building drain to the public sewer or
other place of disposal.
COMBINED SEWER: A sewer receiving both surface runoff and sewage.
GARBAGE: Solid wastes from the domestic and commercial preparation, cooking and
dispensing of food and from the handling, storage and sale of produce.
INDUSTRIAL WASTES: The liquid wastes from industrial manufacturing processes,
trades or businesses as distinct from sanitary sewage.
NATURAL OUTLET: Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other body
of surface or ground water.
PERSON: Any individual, firm, company, association, society, corporation or
group.
pH: The logarithm of the reciprocal of the weight of hydrogen ions in grams per
liter of solution.
PROPERLY SHREDDED GARBAGE: The wastes from the preparation, cooking and
dispensing of food that have been shredded to such a degree that all particles
will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public
sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch (1/2") in any dimension.
PUBLIC SEWER: A sewer in which all owners of abutting properties have equal
rights, and is controlled by a public authority.
SANITARY SEWER: A sewer which carries sewage and to which storm, surface and
ground waters are not intentionally admitted.
SEWAGE: A combination of the water carried wastes from residences, business
buildings, institutions and industrial establishments, together with such
ground, surface and storm waters as may be present.
SEWAGE TREATMENT PLANT: Any arrangement of devices and structures used for
treating sewage.
SEWAGE WORKS: All facilities for collecting, pumping, treating and disposing of
sewage.
SEWER: A pipe or conduit for carrying sewage.
SHALL; MAY: Shall is mandatory; may is permissive.
STORM DRAIN (Sometimes Termed STORM SEWER): A sewer which carries storm and
surface waters and drainage but excludes sewage and industrial wastes, other
than unpolluted cooling water.
SUPERINTENDENT: The superintendent of public works of the city of Plummer or
his authorized deputy, agent or representative.
SUSPENDED SOLIDS: Solids that either float on the surface of or are in
suspension in water, sewage or other liquids and which are removable by
laboratory filtering.
WATERCOURSE: A channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or
intermittently. (Ord. 407, 9-9-2010)
6-7-2: USE OF PUBLIC SEWERS REQUIRED:
   A.   It is unlawful for any person to place, deposit or permit to be
deposited in any unsanitary manner on public or private property within the
city, or in any area under the jurisdiction of the city, any human or animal
excrement, garbage or other objectionable waste, in violation of Title 3,
Chapter 1, Section 9 (Prohibited Animals, Acts and Conditions) or Title 3,
Chapter 4, Section 2 Declaration of Nuisance; Acts Prohibited).
   B.   It is unlawful to discharge to any natural outlet within the city, or
in any area under the jurisdiction of the city, any sewage or other polluted
waters, except where suitable treatment has been provided in accordance with
the subsequent provisions of this chapter.
   C.   It is unlawful to construct or maintain any privy, privy vault, septic
tank, cesspool, or other facility intended or used for the disposal of sewage
on public or private property within the city, or in any area under the
jurisdiction of the city.
   D.   The owner of all houses, buildings or properties used for human
occupancy, employment, recreation or other purposes, situated within the city
and abutting on any street, alley or right of way in which there is now located
or may in the future be located a public sewer of the city, is hereby required,
at his expense, to install suitable toilet facilities therein and to connect
such facilities directly with the proper public sewer in accordance with the
provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 407, 9-9-2010; amd. Ord. 453, 9-12-2019)
6-7-3: PRIVATE SEWAGE DISPOSAL:
   A.   Availability Of Public Sewers:
      1.   At such time as the public sewer becomes available to a property
served by a private sewage disposal system, as provided in section
6-7-2D of this title, a direct connection shall be made to the public sewer in
compliance with this chapter, and any septic tanks, cesspools and similar
private sewage disposal facilities all be abandoned and filled with suitable
material by the property owner within fourteen (14) days of the completion of
the connection of the property to the public sewer system.
      2.   When a public sewer becomes available, the building sewer shall be
connected to said sewer within ninety (90) days, and the private sewage
disposal system shall be cleaned of sludge and filled with clean bank run
gravel or dirt by the property owner within fourteen (14) days of the
completion of the connection of the property to the public sewer system.
   B.   Maintenance In Sanitary Manner: The owner shall operate and maintain
the private sewage disposal facilities in a sanitary manner at all times, at no
expense to the city.
   C.   Extension Of Sewer Main: Upon request and approval by the Mayor and
City Council, the city will extend a sewer main to newly annexed and/or
developed areas, provided that the party or parties making such request pay for
the cost of such extension. (Ord. 407, 9-9-2010; amd. Ord. 453, 9-12-2019)
6-7-4: SEWER USE RATES 1 :
   A.   Sewer use and debt retirement rates shall be as set out in section
6-1-4 of this title.
   B.   No sewer service shall be provided to any structure, home, building or
other unit until such time as the owner thereof shall make application to the
city therefor. (Ord. 407, 9-9-2010)
 
Notes
1 1. See chapter 4 of this title.
6-7-5: BUILDING SEWERS AND CONNECTIONS:
   A.   No unauthorized person shall uncover, make any connection with or
opening into, use, alter or disturb any public sewer or appurtenance thereof
without first obtaining a written permit from the superintendent.
   B.   A hook up and capitalization fee shall be required during application
and prior to sewer connection. This shall cover the connection to the sewer
main and up to the property line. The application must include plans,
specifications or other information considered pertinent in the judgment of the
superintendent. The hookup and capitalization fee shall be in addition to any
cost associated with extending the sewer main to newly annexed and/or developed
areas, as provided for in section
6-7-3C of this title.
   C.   All costs and expense incident to the installation and connection of
the building sewer from the property line to the building shall be borne by the
owner. The owner shall indemnify the city from any loss or damage that may
directly or indirectly be occasioned by the installation of the building sewer.
   D.   A separate and independent building sewer shall be provided for every
building.
   E.   Old building sewers may be used in connection with new buildings only
when they are found, on examination and test by the superintendent, to meet all
requirements of this chapter. Such examination shall only be made after
application and payment of an inspection fee to the city.
   F.   The size, slope, alignment, materials of construction of a building
sewer and the methods to be used in excavating, placing of the pipe, jointing,
testing and backfilling the trench shall all conform to the requirements of the
building and plumbing codes or other applicable rules and regulations of the
city. In the absence of code provisions or in amplification thereof, the
materials and procedures set forth in appropriate specifications of the ASTM
and "WPCF Manual Of Practice No. 9" shall apply.
   G.   Whenever possible, the building sewer shall be brought to the building
at an elevation below the basement floor. In all buildings in which any
building drain is too low to permit gravity flow to the public sewer, sanitary
sewage carried by such building drain shall be lifted by an approved means and
discharged to the building sewer at the owner's expense or grade restrictions
may be imposed upon the construction design of the building.
   H.   No person shall make connection of roof downspouts, exterior foundation
drains, cellar drains, sump pumps, areaway drains or other sources of surface
runoff or groundwater to a building sewer or building drain which in turn is
connected directly or indirectly to a public sanitary sewer.
   I.   The connection of the building sewer into the public sewer shall
conform to the requirements of the building and plumbing codes or other
applicable rules and regulations of the city or the procedures set forth in
appropriate specifications of the ASTM and the "WPCF Manual Of Practice No. 9".
All such connections shall be made gastight and watertight. Any deviation from
the prescribed procedures and materials must be approved by the superintendent
before installation.
   J.   Provisions for the connection of manufactured homes, or any other
mobile units to the public sewer system may be made by a pipe connected to the
sanitary sewer system in compliance with this section. When not connected to a
mobile unit such system must be sealed with a cap, sealing plug or comparable
device in such manner as to stop any substance or gas from entering or leaving
the sanitary sewer system.
   K.   The applicant for the building sewer permit shall notify the
superintendent when the building sewer is ready for inspection and connection
to the public sewer. The connection shall be made under the supervision of the
superintendent or his representative.
   L.   All excavations for building sewer installation shall be adequately
guarded with barricades and lights so as to protect the public from hazard.
Streets, sidewalks, parkways and other public property disturbed in the course
of the work shall be restored in a manner satisfactory to the city.
   M.   No person shall disconnect or abandon any sewage connection without
first notifying the superintendent. After such notification, the connection may
be disconnected and sealed in such a manner so as to prevent the passage of any
substance, gas or odor into or out of said sewage line. Said patch or sealing
shall not in any way impede the flow of sewage within the sewage line and shall
be of sufficient thickness, strength and design to equal the sewage line. The
superintendent shall be notified upon completion of sealing and any excavation
for such a sealing shall be left open for sufficient time for the
superintendent to inspect the same. (Ord. 407, 9-9-2010; amd. Ord. 453, 9-12-
2019)
6-7-6: USE OF THE PUBLIC SEWERS:
   A.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any stormwater,
surface water, groundwater, roof runoff, subsurface drainage, uncontaminated
cooling water or unpolluted industrial process waters to any sanitary sewer.
   B.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the
following described waters or wastes to any public sewers:
      1.   Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil or other flammable or
explosive solid or gas.
      2.   Any waters or wastes containing toxic or poisonous solids, liquids
or gases of sufficient quantity, either singly or by interaction with other
wastes, to injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process, constitute a
hazard to humans or animals, create a public nuisance or create any hazard in
the receiving waters of the sewage treatment plant including, but not limited
to, cyanides in excess of two milligrams per liter (2 mg/l) as CN in the wastes
as discharged to the public sewer.
      3.   Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5 or having any other
corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard to structures, equipment
and personnel of the sewage works.
      4.   Solid or viscous substances in quantities or of such size capable of
causing obstruction to the flow in sewers or other interference with the proper
operation of the sewage works such as, but not limited to, ashes, cinders,
sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags, feathers, tar, plastics, wood,
unground garbage, whole blood, paunch manure, hair and fleshings, entrails and
paper dishes, cups, milk containers, etc., either whole or ground by garbage
grinders.
      5.   Floatable oils, fats, or grease.
   C.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any substances,
materials, waters or wastes if it appears likely, in the opinion of the
superintendent, that such wastes can harm either the sewers, sewage treatment
process or equipment, have an adverse effect on the receiving stream or can
otherwise endanger life, limb, public property or constitute a nuisance. In
forming his opinion as to the acceptability of these wastes, the superintendent
will give consideration to such factors as to quantities of subject wastes in
relation to flows and velocities in the sewers, materials of construction of
the sewers, nature of the sewage treatment process, capacity of the sewage
treatment plant, degree of treatability of wastes in the sewage treatment plant
and other pertinent factors. The substances prohibited are:
      1.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred
fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150ºF) (65ºC);
      2.   Any water or waste containing fats, wax, grease or oils, emulsified
or not, in excess of one hundred (100) mg/l or containing substances which may
solidify or become viscous at temperatures between thirty two degrees
Fahrenheit (32ºF) and one hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150ºF) (0º and
65ºC);
      3.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. The installation
and operation of any garbage grinder with a motor three-fourths (¾) horsepower
or greater shall be subject to review and approval of the superintendent;
      4.   Any waters or wastes containing strong acid iron pickling wastes or
concentrated plating solutions, whether neutralized or not;
      5.   Any waters or wastes containing iron, chromium, copper, zinc, and
similar objectionable or toxic substances; or wastes exerting an excessive
chlorine requirement, to such degree that any such material received in the
composite sewage at the sewage treatment works exceeds the limits established
by the superintendent for such material;
      6.   Any waters or wastes containing phenols or other taste producing or
odor producing substances, in such concentrations exceeding limits which may be
established by the superintendent as necessary, after treatment of the
composite sewage, to meet the requirements of the state, federal or other
public agencies or jurisdiction for such discharge to the receiving waters;
      7.   Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half-life or
concentrations as may exceed limits established by the superintendent in
compliance with applicable state or federal regulations;
      8.   Any waters or wastes having pH in excess of nine and five-tenths
(9.5);
      9.   Materials which exert or cause:
         a.   Unusual concentrations of inert suspended solids, such as, but
not limited to, fullers earth, lime slurries, and lime residues, or of
dissolved, such as, but not limited to, sodium chloride or sodium sulfate;
         b.   Excessive discoloration, such as, but not limited to, dye wastes
and vegetable tanning solutions;
         c.   Unusual BOD, chemical oxygen demand, or chlorine requirements in
such quantities as to constitute a significant load on the sewage treatment
works;
         d.   Unusual volume of flow or concentrations of wastes constituting
"slugs" as defined in section
8-1-2 of this title;
      10.   Waters or wastes containing substances which are not amendable to
treatment or reduction by the sewage treatment processes employed, or are
amenable to treatment only to such degree that the sewage treatment plant
effluent cannot meet the requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction
over discharge to the receiving waters.
   D.   If any waters or wastes are discharged or are proposed to be discharged
to the public sewers which, in the judgment of the superintendent, may have a
deleterious effect upon the sewage works, processes, equipment or receiving
waters or which otherwise create a hazard to life or constitute a public
nuisance, the superintendent may:
      1.   Reject the wastes.
      2.   Require pretreatment to an acceptable condition for discharge to the
public sewers.
      3.   Require control over the quantities and rates of discharge.
      4.   Require payment to cover the added cost of handling and treating the
wastes not covered by existing taxes or sewer charge under the provision of
subsection G of this section.
   If the superintendent permits the pretreatment or equalization of water
flows, the design and installation of the plants and equipment shall be subject
to the review and approval of the superintendent and subject to the
requirements of all applicable codes, ordinances and laws.
   E.   Control Manhole: When required by the superintendent, the owner of any
property serviced by a building sewer carrying industrial wastes shall install
a suitable control manhole together with such necessary meters and other
appurtenances in the building sewer to facilitate observation, sampling and
measurement of the wastes. Such manhole, when required, shall be accessibly and
safely located, and shall be constructed in accordance with plans approved by
the superintendent. The manhole shall be installed by the owner at his expense,
and shall be maintained by him so as to be safe an accessible at all times.
   F.   Measurements, Tests And Analysis: All measurements, tests and analyses
of the characteristics of waters and wastes to which reference is made in this
chapter shall be determined in accordance with the latest edition of "Standard
Methods For The Examination Of Water and Wastewater," published by the American
Public Health Association, and shall be determined at the control manhole
provided, or upon suitable samples taken at said control manhole. In the event
that no special manhole has been required, the control manhole shall be
considered to be the nearest downstream manhole in the public sewer to the
point at which the building sewer is connected. Sampling shall be carried out
by customarily accepted methods to reflect the effect of constituents upon the
sewage works and to determine the existence of hazards to life, limb and
property. The particular analyses involved will determine whether a 24-hour
composite of all outfalls of a premises is appropriate or whether a grab sample
or samples should be taken. Normally, but not always, BOD and suspended solids
analyses are obtained from 24-hour composites of all outfalls whereas pHs are
determine from periodic grab samples.)
   G.   Special Agreement: No statement contained in this section shall be
construed as preventing any special agreement or arrangement between the city
and any industrial concern whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or
character may be accepted by the city for treatment, subject to payment
therefor, by the industrial concern. (Ord. 407, 9-9-2010; amd. Ord. 453, 9-12-
2019)
6-7-7: GREASE, OIL OR SEDIMENT SEPARATORS:
   A.   Separators Required: Grease, oil or sediment separators shall be
provided as part of the building sewer when required by the international
building or international plumbing code, or in the opinion of the
superintendent they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid wastes
containing floatable oils, fat, flammable wastes, sand or other harmful
ingredients as restricted herein; except that such separators shall not be
required under named circumstances.
   B.   Type And Location: All separators shall be of a type and capacity
approved by the superintendent and shall be located as to be readily and easily
accessible for cleaning and inspection.
   C.   Maintenance Of Separators; Records Of Disposal: In the maintaining of
these separators, the owner shall be responsible for the proper removal and
disposal by appropriate means of the captivated material and shall maintain
records of the dates and means of disposal which are subject to review by the
superintendent. Any removal and hauling of the collected materials not
performed by the owner's personnel must be performed by currently licensed
disposal firms.
   D.   Establishments Requiring Separators: Establishments requiring these
separators include, but are not limited to, restaurants, cafeterias, taverns,
extended care facilities, automotive repair shops, service stations and car
washes. Where pretreatment of flow equalizing facilities is required for any
grease, oil or sediment separators, waters or wastes, they shall be constructed
and maintained continuously in satisfactory and effective operation by and at
the expense of the sewer user.
   E.   Observation, Sampling And Measurement Of Waste: When required by the
superintendent, an industrial discharger shall install a suitable structure
together with such necessary meters and other appurtenances in the building
sewer to facilitate observation, sampling and measurement of the wastes. Such
structures, when required, shall be accessibly and safely located and shall be
constructed in accordance with plans approved by the superintendent. The
structure shall be installed by the discharger at its expense, shall be
maintained by the discharger at its expense and shall be maintained by the
discharger so as to be safe and accessible at all times. (Ord. 407, 9-9-2010)
6-7-8: POWERS AND AUTHORITY OF INSPECTORS:
   A.   The superintendent and other duly authorized employees of the city
bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter all
properties for the purposes of inspection, observation, measurement, sampling
and testing in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. The
superintendent or his representatives shall have no authority to inquire into
any processes, including metallurgical, chemical, oil, refining, ceramic, paper
or other industries, beyond that point having a direct bearing on the kind and
source of discharge to the sewers or waterways or facilities for waste
treatment.
   B.   The superintendent and other duly authorized employees of the city
bearing proper credentials and identification may require a user to provide
information needed to determine compliance with this chapter. These
requirements may include:
      1.   Wastewater discharge peak rate and volume over a specified time
period.
      2.   Chemical analyses of wastewaters.
      3.   Information on raw materials, processes and products affecting
wastewater volume and quality.
      4.   Quantity and disposition of specific liquid sludge, oil, solvent or
other materials important to sewer use control.
      5.   A plot plan of sewers on the user's property showing sewer and
pretreatment facility location.
      6.   Details of wastewater pretreatment facilities.
      7.   Details of systems to prevent and control the losses of materials
through spills to the public sewer.
   C.   The superintendent and other duly authorized employees of the city
bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter all
private properties through which the city holds a duly negotiated easement for
the purposes of, but not limited to, inspection, observation, measurement,
sampling, repair and maintenance of any portion of the sewage works lying
within said easement. All entry and subsequent work, if any, on said easement,
shall be done in full accordance with the terms of the duly negotiated easement
pertaining to the private property involved. (Ord. 407, 9-9-2010; amd. Ord.
453, 9-12-2019)
6-7-9: PENALTIES:
   A.   Any person found to be violating any provision of this chapter shall be
served by the city with written notice stating the nature of the violation and
providing a reasonable time limit for the satisfactory correction thereof. The
offender shall, within the period of time stated in such notice, permanently
cease all violations. In the event that a violation consists of a discharge of
any sewage, including ground, surface or storm water, either directly or
indirectly, into the public sewer system, or of a failure to permit inspection
by the superintendent and other duly authorized employees of the city in
relation thereto, then a fine of One Hundred Dollars ($100.00), per day, shall
be assessed to the owner or occupant of the property, until such correction is
made. The fine provided for herein shall be assessed to the owner or occupant
of the property on the sewer bill, in addition to any other fees for sewer
services.
   B.   Any person who shall continue any violation beyond the time limit
provided for in subsection A of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor
and, on conviction thereof, subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each day in which such violation continues after conviction
shall constitute a separate offense.
   C.   Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall become
liable to the city for any expense, loss or damage occasioned the city by
reason of such violation. (Ord. 407, 9-9-2010; amd. Ord. 453, 9-12-2019)
6-7-10: PROTECTION FROM DAMAGE:
No unauthorized person shall maliciously, willfully or negligently break,
damage, destroy, uncover, deface or tamper with any structure, appurtenance or
equipment which is a part of the sewage works. Any person violating this
provision shall be subject to immediate arrest under charge of disorderly
conduct. (Ord. 453, 9-12-2019)
TITLE 7
BUILDING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
BUILDING CODES
SECTION:
7-1-1: Adoption Of Codes By Reference
7-1-2: Administration Of Codes
7-1-3: Compliance Required
7-1-4: Appeal From Administrative Rulings
7-1-5: Penalty
7-1-1: ADOPTION OF CODES BY REFERENCE:
   A.   Codes Adopted: The City Council of the City of Plummer, Idaho, hereby
adopts and enacts by reference, the following codes:
      1.   International Building Code, 2018 edition, with Idaho amendments,
collectively named the Building Code 2018 of Idaho, as adopted and amended by
